$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c} \exists \mu \in [M] \ s.t. \\ \tilde{A}_{0}^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \neq \tilde{B}_{1}^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \end{array}\right. \left. \begin{array}{c} (Q_{b}^{\mu}, \operatorname{st}_{b}^{\mu}) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr}.Q_{D^{\mu}}(\{z^{\mu}\}) \ for \ \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \{A_{b}^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_{1}(\operatorname{aux}, \{S_{b}^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}), \\ where \ S_{0}^{\mu} \coloneqq Q_{0}^{\mu} \cup Q_{1}^{\mu} \ and \ S_{1}^{\mu} \coloneqq Q_{1}^{\mu} \\ \tilde{A}_{b}^{\mu} \coloneqq \operatorname{SelfCorr}.\operatorname{Rec}_{d}(\operatorname{st}_{b}^{\mu}, A_{b}^{\mu}) \ for \ \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \tilde{B}_{1}^{\mu} \coloneqq \operatorname{SelfCorr}.\operatorname{Rec}_{d}(\operatorname{st}_{1}^{\mu}, A_{0}^{\mu}) \ for \ \forall \mu \in [M] \end{array}\right] \geq 1/\operatorname{poly}(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.6}$$

*Proof*. Since Equation (E.5) holds, the CNS of  $\mathcal{A}_1$  (which is inherited from the CNS of C.Dec<sub>1</sub>\*) implies that we can obtain Equation (E.6) by showing

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c} \forall \mu \in [M], \\ \tilde{A}_{1}^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) = \tilde{B}_{1}^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \end{array}\right. \left(\begin{array}{c} (Q_{b}^{\mu}, \operatorname{st}_{b}^{\mu}) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr}. Q_{D^{\mu}}(\{z^{\mu}\}) \text{ for } \forall b \in \{0, 1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \{A_{b}^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0, 1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathcal{R}_{1}(\operatorname{aux}, \{S_{b}^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0, 1\}, \mu \in [M]}), \\ \text{where } S_{0}^{\mu} \coloneqq Q_{0}^{\mu} \cup Q_{1}^{\mu} \text{ and } S_{1}^{\mu} \coloneqq Q_{1}^{\mu} \\ \tilde{A}_{b}^{\mu} \coloneqq \operatorname{SelfCorr}. \operatorname{Rec}_{d}(\operatorname{st}_{b}^{\mu}, A_{b}^{\mu}) \text{ for } \forall b \in \{0, 1\}, \mu \in [M] \end{array}\right] \geq 1 - \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.7}$$

Hence, we focus on showing Equation (E.7).

First, we remark that from the construction of SelfCorr, the two values  $\tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu})$  and  $\tilde{B}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu})$  in Equation (E.7) are sampled in the following manner.

- 1. For  $\forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]$ , choose  $\lambda$  random lines  $L_{b,1}^{\mu}, \dots, L_{b,\lambda}^{\mu} : \mathbf{F} \to D^{\mu}$  such that each  $L \in \{L_{b,1}^{\mu}, \dots, L_{b,\lambda}^{\mu}\}$  satisfies  $L(0) = \mathbf{z}^{\mu}$ . Let  $Q_b^{\mu} \coloneqq \{L_{b,j}^{\mu}(t)\}_{j \in [\lambda], t \in \mathbf{F} \setminus \{0\}}$ .
- 2. Run  $\{A_b^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1(\text{aux}, \{S_b^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}), \text{ where } S_0^{\mu} \coloneqq Q_0^{\mu} \cup Q_1^{\mu} \text{ and } S_1^{\mu} \coloneqq Q_1^{\mu}.$
- 3. For  $\forall \mu \in [M]$ , check that there exists  $c_1^{\mu} \in F$  such that

<span id="page-31-2"></span><span id="page-31-1"></span>
$$\left|\left\{j\in[\lambda]\;\middle|\;\operatorname{Recon}_d\left(\left\{A_1^\mu(L_{1,j}^\mu(t))\right\}_{t\in F\setminus\{0\}}\right)=c_1^\mu\right\}\right|\geq 0.9\lambda\ .$$

Let  $\tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) := c_1^{\mu}$  if such  $c_1^{\mu}$  exists, and let  $\tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) := \bot$  otherwise.

4. For  $\forall \mu \in [M]$ , check that there exists  $d_1^{\mu} \in F$  such that

$$\left|\left\{j \in [\lambda] \mid \mathsf{Recon}_d\left(\left\{A_0^\mu(L_{1,j}^\mu(t))\right\}_{t \in F\setminus\{0\}}\right) = d_1^\mu\right\}\right| \ge 0.9\lambda .$$

Let  $\tilde{B}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) := d_1^{\mu}$  if such  $d_1^{\mu}$  exists, and let  $\tilde{B}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) := \bot$  otherwise.

{32}------------------------------------------------

In what follows, we always consider probability over this sampling.

Note that due to Equation (E.4) and Lemma K.1 (Correctness of SelfCorr) in Section K.1 (which roughly says that SelfCorr outputs  $\bot$  only with negligible probability for any adversary that passes the low-degree test), we have  $\tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \neq \bot$  and  $\tilde{B}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \neq \bot$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$  except with negligible probability. From the construction of Recon, this implies that except with negligible probability, we have

$$\left| \left\{ j \in [\lambda] \mid \bot \notin \left\{ A_1^{\mu}(L_{1,j}^{\mu}(t)) \right\}_{t \in F \setminus \{0\}} \right\} \right| \ge 0.9\lambda$$

and

$$\left| \left\{ j \in [\lambda] \mid \bot \notin \left\{ A_0^{\mu}(L_{1,j}^{\mu}(t)) \right\}_{t \in F \setminus \{0\}} \right\} \right| \ge 0.9\lambda$$

for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$ . Combined with Equation (E.3), these two imply that except with negligible probability, we have

$$\left| \left\{ j \in [\lambda] \mid A_0^{\mu}(L_{1,j}^{\mu}(t)) = A_1^{\mu}(L_{1,j}^{\mu}(t)) \neq \bot \text{ for } \forall t \in \mathbf{F} \setminus \{0\} \right\} \right| \ge 0.8\lambda$$
 (E.8)

for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$ . Thus, from a union bound, we have  $\tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \neq \bot$ ,  $\tilde{B}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \neq \bot$ , and Equation (E.8) for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$  except with negligible probability. From the definitions of  $\tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu})$ ,  $\tilde{B}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu})$ , this implies that we have  $\tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) = \tilde{B}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu})$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$  except with negligible probability, as desired.

**Claim E.3.** Let  $\mathcal{A}_2$  be the following algorithm.

- <span id="page-32-1"></span>• On input (aux,  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$ ):
  - 1.  $Run\{A_h^{\mu}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}\leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1(\mathsf{aux},\{Q_h^{\mu}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}), where Q_0^{\mu}\coloneqq Q^{\mu} \ and \ Q_1^{\mu}\coloneqq\emptyset.$
  - 2. Output  $\{A_0^{\mu}\}_{{\mu}\in[M]}$ .

Then, for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$ , there exist  $\text{aux} \in \{0, 1\}^{\text{poly}(\lambda)}$  and  $z^1 \in D^1, \dots, z^M \in D^M$  such that

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c|c} \forall \mu \in [M], & \left(Q^{\mu}, \operatorname{st}^{\mu}\right) \leftarrow \operatorname{LD-Test.Q}_{D^{\mu}} for \ \mu \in [M] \\ \operatorname{LD-Test.D}_{d,3\zeta}(\operatorname{st}^{\mu}, A^{\mu}) = 1 & \left\{A^{\mu}\right\}_{\mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathcal{H}_{2}(\operatorname{aux}, \{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}) \end{array}\right] \geq 1 - \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$$

and

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c} \exists \mu \in [M] \ s.t. \\ \tilde{A}_0^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \neq \tilde{A}_1^{\mu}(z^{\mu}) \end{array} \right| \begin{array}{c} (Q_b^{\mu}, \operatorname{st}_b^{\mu}) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr}. Q_{D^{\mu}}(\{z^{\mu}\}) \ for \ \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \{A^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathcal{H}_2(\operatorname{aux}, \{Q_0^{\mu} \cup Q_1^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}) \\ \tilde{A}_b^{\mu} := \operatorname{SelfCorr}. \operatorname{Rec}_d(\operatorname{st}_b^{\mu}, A^{\mu}) \ for \ \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \end{array} \right] \geq 1/\operatorname{poly}(\lambda) \ ,$$

where  $d := m_{Io}|\mathbf{H}|$  and  $D^{\mu} := D(X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}).$ 

*Proof*. This claim follows from Claim E.1, Claim E.2, and the assumption that  $C_1^*$  is CNS (which implies that  $\mathcal{A}_1$  is CNS), since the latter implies that the output of  $\mathcal{A}_2(\mathsf{aux}, \{Q_0^\mu \cup Q_1^\mu\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  is computationally indistinguishable from that of  $\mathcal{A}_1(\mathsf{aux}, \{S_b^\mu\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]})$ , where  $S_0^\mu \coloneqq Q_0^\mu \cup Q_1^\mu$  and  $S_1^\mu \coloneqq Q_1^\mu$ .

Clearly, Claim E.3 contradicts with (the straightforward parallel version of) Lemma K.2 (Consistency of SelfCorr). This concludes the proof of Lemma E.2.

#### **E.3** Proof of Soundness

We prove the soundness against cheating adversaries that are no-signaling and well-behaving in the following sense.

<span id="page-32-0"></span>**Definition 19** (No-signaling committer-prover). *A cheating committer-prover*  $C_1^* = (C.Com_1^*, C.Prv_1^*)$  *against*  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  *is*  $\kappa_{\text{max}}$ -CNS *if*  $C.Prv_1^*(st_C, \cdot)$  *is*  $\kappa_{\text{max}}$ -CNS *for*  $\forall (st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_1^*, R.Com_1 \rangle$ .

**Definition 20** (Well-behaving committer-prover). A cheating committer-prover  $C_1^* = (C.Com_1^*, C.Prv_1^*)$  against  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  is well-behaving if both of the following hold.

1. Consistency on  $D(X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu})$ : For  $\forall \lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,  $\forall \{Q_0^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, \{Q_1^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]} \subseteq (D(X))^{M^2}$ ,  $\forall \alpha,\beta,\gamma,\delta \in [M]$  such that  $\exists \xi \in \{\alpha,\beta\} \cap \{\gamma,\delta\}$ , and  $\forall \mathbf{q} \in Q_0^{\alpha:\beta} \cap Q_1^{\gamma:\delta} \cap D(X_{1,\text{in}}^{\xi})$ , it holds

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{l} \pi_0^{*\alpha:\beta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \neq \bot \\ \wedge \pi_1^{*\gamma:\delta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \neq \bot \\ \wedge \pi_0^{*\alpha:\beta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \neq \pi_1^{*\gamma:\delta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \end{array} \right] \quad \left( \begin{array}{l} (\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C.Com}_1^*, \mathsf{R.Com}_1 \rangle \\ (f, \{\pi_0^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{Q_0^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \\ (f, \{\pi_1^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{Q_1^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ .$$

{33}------------------------------------------------

2. Consistency on  $D(X^{\mu})$ : For  $\forall \lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,  $\forall \{Q^{\mu;\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]} \subseteq (D(X))^{M^2}$ ,  $\forall \alpha, \beta, \gamma, \delta \in [M]$  such that  $\exists \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\} \cap \{\gamma, \delta\}$ , and  $\forall \mathbf{q} \in Q^{\alpha:\beta} \cap Q^{\gamma:\delta} \cap D(X^{\xi})$ , it holds

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c} \pi^{*\alpha:\beta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \neq \bot \\ \wedge \, \pi^{*\gamma:\delta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \neq \bot \\ \wedge \, \pi^{*\alpha:\beta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \neq \pi^{*\gamma:\delta}(\boldsymbol{q}) \end{array} \right] \quad \left( \operatorname{st}_{C}, \operatorname{com} \right) \leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_{1}^{*}, \operatorname{R.Com}_{1} \rangle \\ (f, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\operatorname{st}_{C}, \{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \end{array} \right] \leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) .$$

Remark 5 (Intuition of well-behaving adversaries). Roughly speaking, the above definition of well-behaving adversaries guarantees the following. Recall that in  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$ , the  $(\mu, \nu)$ -th instance of (PCP.P, PCP.V) is used for proving consistency of a pair of views (view<sup> $\mu$ </sup>, view<sup> $\nu$ </sup>), and the receiver expects that it can query to an LDE  $X^{\mu\nu}$  of a satisfying assignment to the variables in  $\varphi_f^{\mu\nu}$ . Also, recall that the receiver expects that through  $X^{\mu\nu}$ , it can query to an LDE  $X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$  of an assignment to the variables indexed by  $I_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$ , and as remarked in Remark 3, the assignment to these variables should be the initial state of  $P^{\mu}$  (which is committed in the commit phase). Also, recall that the receiver expects that through  $X^{\mu\nu}$ , it can query to an LDE  $X^{\mu}$  of an assignment to the variables indexed by  $I^{\mu}$ , and as remarked in Remark 3, the assignment to these variables should depend only on view<sup> $\mu$ </sup>, meaning that the same values should be assigned to these variables in the  $(\mu, \nu)$ -th instance of (PCP.P, PCP.V) and in the  $(\mu, \xi)$ -th one. Now, the first condition of well-behaving adversaries guarantees that once the commit phase is completed, the adversary does not give different answers to the queries to  $X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$  in different invocations. Regarding the second condition, it guarantees that once the commit phase is completed, the adversary does not give different answers to the queries to  $X^{\mu}$  in different instances of (PCP.P, PCP.V) in a single invocation.

The formal statement of the soundness of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  is given below.

**Lemma E.3.** There exists a polynomial  $\kappa_{\text{prv}}$  such that the following holds. Let  $\epsilon_{\text{SND}}$  be any negligible function,  $E_1$  be the extractor in Algorithm 8, and  $C_1^* = (\text{C.Com}_1^*, \text{C.Prv}_1^*)$  be any well-behaving  $\kappa_{\text{prv}}$ -CNS cheating committer-prover against  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$ . Then, for every  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the following soundness condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_1^*, \text{R.Com}_1 \rangle$ .

<span id="page-33-0"></span>• Soundness Condition: If it holds

<span id="page-33-2"></span>
$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_1; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_1(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \ge 1 - \epsilon_{\scriptscriptstyle SND}(\lambda) \ , \tag{E.9}$$

then there exists  $x_{com}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that

$$\forall i \in [n], \Pr\left[x_i = x_i^* \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_1^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_1(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle\right] \ge 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \tag{E.10}$$

and

<span id="page-33-5"></span><span id="page-33-4"></span>
$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c|c} b = 1 & (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_1; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ h \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_1(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.11}$$

#### **Algorithm 8** Extractor $E_1$ (against $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$ )

**Input:** com, i, and  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\subset D(X^1_{1,\mathsf{in}})\times\cdots\times D(X^M_{1,\mathsf{in}})$ 

- 1. Run  $(f, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$ , where each  $Q^{\mu:\nu}$  is defined as  $Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq Q^{\mu}$  if  $\mu = \nu$  and  $Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset$  otherwise.
- <span id="page-33-1"></span>2. Output  $\{\tilde{X}^{*,\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  as the decommitment, where  $\tilde{X}^{*,\mu:\mu}:=\pi^{*,\mu:\mu}$ .

We directly go to the formal proof. An overview of the proof is given in Section 4.

*Proof*. We let  $\kappa_{\text{prv}} = \kappa_0 \cdot \kappa_{\text{max}}$ , where  $\kappa_0, \kappa_{\text{max}}$  are the polynomials that are given in Lemma D.4. Fix any  $\epsilon_{\text{SND}}$  and  $C_1^* = (\text{C.Com}_1^*, \text{C.Prv}_1^*)$  such that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , Equation (E.9) holds with non-negligible probability over the choice of (st<sub>C</sub>, com) ← ⟨C.Com<sub>1</sub>\*, R.Com<sub>1</sub>⟩ (if no such  $\epsilon_{\text{SND}}$  and  $C_1^*$  exist, the lemma holds trivially), and let Λ be the set of such  $\lambda$ .

#### Step 0: showing consistency properties on self-corrected C.Prv\*.

First, we make preliminary observations on SelfCorr. Specifically, we observe that the consistency conditions of well-behaving adversaries (Definition 20) hold even on the outputs of SelfCorr.

<span id="page-33-3"></span>**Claim E.4** (Consistency on  $D(X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu})$ ). For every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ , the following holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_1^*, \text{R.Com}_1 \rangle$ .

{34}------------------------------------------------

• If Equation (E.9) holds, then there exists  $\{(x_1^{\mu}, \dots, x_{N_{10}}^{\mu})\}_{\mu \in [M]} \in (\{0, 1\}^{N_{10}})^M$  such that for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{1 \text{ in}}^{\xi}$ ,

$$\Pr\begin{bmatrix} A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^{*}) = x_{i^{*}}^{\xi} & (Q, \operatorname{st}) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr.Q}_{D(X_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\xi})}(\{i^{*}\}) \\ (f, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\operatorname{st}_{C}, \{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}), \\ where \ Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \ for \ \forall (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \ and \ Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq Q \\ A^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \operatorname{SelfCorr.Rec}_{m_{\omega}|H|}(\operatorname{st}, \pi^{*\alpha:\beta}) \end{bmatrix} \geq 1 - \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.12}$$

*Proof*. Fix any  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ .

First, we observe that, by using the argument in the proof of Lemma E.2, we can show that with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\operatorname{st}_C,\operatorname{com}) \leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_1^*,\operatorname{R.Com}_1\rangle$ , if Equation (E.9) holds, then there exists  $\{(x_1^\mu,\ldots,x_{N_{10}}^\mu)\}_{\mu\in[M]}\in (F^{N_{10}})^M$  such that for  $\forall \alpha,\beta\in[M],\ \forall \xi\in\{\alpha,\beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^*\in\mathcal{I}_{1,\mathrm{in}}^\xi$ , we have Equation (E.12). To see this, first observe that since the proof verification includes the low-degree test for  $D(X_{1,\mathrm{in}}^\xi)$ , Equation (E.9) implies  $\forall \alpha,\beta\in[M],\ \forall \xi\in\{\alpha,\beta\}$ ,

$$\Pr\begin{bmatrix} b_{\text{\tiny LD}} = 1 & (Q, \text{st}) \leftarrow \text{LD-Test.Q}_{D(X_{1,\text{in}}^{\xi})} \\ (f, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \text{C.Prv}_1^*(\text{st}_C, \{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \text{ and } Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq Q \\ b_{\text{\tiny LD}} \coloneqq \text{LD-Test.D}_{m:\alpha|H|,\zeta}(\text{st}, \pi^{*\alpha:\beta}) \end{bmatrix} \geq 1 - \text{negl}(\lambda) \ .$$

From this observation, it follows that given Equation (E.9), we can argue as in Lemma E.2 to show that for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{1, \text{in}}^{\xi}$ , the value of  $A^{\alpha; \beta}(i^*)$  is unique when computed as in Equation (E.12). Second, since the prove phase of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  is just parallel executions of (PCP.P, PCP.V), the everywhere local con-

Second, since the prove phase of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  is just parallel executions of (PCP.P, PCP.V), the everywhere local consistency of SelfCorr (Claim D.4) and Lemma K.3 in Section K.1 (which guarantees that the values recovered from SelfCorr<sub> $m_{10}|H|,D(X_{1,in}^{\xi})$ </sub> and SelfCorr<sub> $m_{1}|H|,D(X)$ </sub> are equal) imply that for any (st<sub>C</sub>, com)  $\leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_{1}^{*}, \text{R.Com}_{1} \rangle$ , if Equation (E.9) holds, then for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M], \forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{1,in}^{\xi}$ , we have  $\Pr\left[A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = 0 \lor A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = 1\right] \geq 1 - \text{negl}(\lambda)$ , where the probability is taken as in Equation (E.12).<sup>32</sup>

By combining the above two, we obtain the claim.

**Claim E.5** (Consistency on  $D(X^{\mu})$ ). For every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ , the following holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com}) \leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_1^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_1 \rangle$ .

<span id="page-34-1"></span>• If Equation (E.9) holds, then  $\forall \alpha, \beta, \gamma, \delta \in [M]$  such that  $\exists \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\} \cap \{\gamma, \delta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in I^{\xi}$ ,

$$\Pr\left[ A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = A^{\gamma:\delta}(i^*) \right] \begin{array}{l} (Q_0, \operatorname{st}_0) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr}. \mathsf{Q}_{D(X^{\xi})}(\{i^*\}) \\ (Q_1, \operatorname{st}_1) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr}. \mathsf{Q}_{D(X^{\xi})}(\{i^*\}) \\ (f, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Prv}_1^*(\operatorname{st}_C, \{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}), \\ where \ Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \ for \ \forall (\mu,\nu) \notin \{(\alpha,\beta),(\gamma,\delta)\}, \\ Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq Q_0, \ and \ Q^{\gamma:\delta} \coloneqq Q_1 \\ A^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \operatorname{SelfCorr}. \operatorname{Rec}_{(m-1)|H|}(\operatorname{st}_0, \pi^{*\alpha:\beta}) \\ A^{\gamma:\delta} \coloneqq \operatorname{SelfCorr}. \operatorname{Rec}_{(m-1)|H|}(\operatorname{st}_1, \pi^{*\gamma:\delta}) \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.13}$$

<span id="page-34-0"></span>

*Proof*. This claim can be proven similarly to Lemma E.2.

Next, we introduce a definition that we use in the rest of the proof.

**Definition 21.** For any  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ , we say that  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$  is good if under the condition that  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$  is output by  $(\operatorname{C.Com}_1^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_1)$ , the following hold.

- Equation (E.9) holds.
- There exists  $\{(x_1^{\mu},\ldots,x_{N_{lo}}^{\mu})\}_{\mu\in[M]}\in(\{0,1\}^{N_{lo}})^M$  such that Equation (E.12) holds for  $\forall \alpha,\beta\in[M],\ \forall \xi\in\{\alpha,\beta\},$  and  $\forall i^*\in\mathcal{I}_{1.\text{in}}^{\xi}.$
- Equation (E.13) holds for  $\forall \alpha, \beta, \gamma, \delta \in [M]$  such that  $\exists \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\} \cap \{\gamma, \delta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}^{\xi}$ .

Furthermore, for any  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and any good  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$ , we say that  $\{(\operatorname{st}_0^\mu, \operatorname{i-msgs}_1^\mu)\}_{\mu \in [M]} = \{(x_1^\mu, \dots, x_{N_{lo}}^\mu)\}_{\mu \in [M]} \in (\{0, 1\}^{N_{lo}})^M$  is the (unique) good MPC initial state if Equation (E.12) holds on  $\{(x_1^\mu, \dots, x_{N_{lo}}^\mu)\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{1,\text{in}}^\xi$ .

From Claim E.4 and Claim E.5, it follows that for proving Lemma E.3, it suffices to show that for any good ( $\operatorname{st}_C$ ,  $\operatorname{com}$ ), there exists  $x_{\operatorname{com}}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that Equations (E.10) and (E.11) hold.

 $<sup>^{32}</sup>$ The everywhere local consistency implies that if the three variables of a clause in  $\varphi_f^{\alpha;\beta}$  are assigned by SelfCorr, the values assigned to them are 0 or 1 with overwhelming probability. Then, CNS implies that even when each of the three variables is assigned by SelfCorr individually, the value assigned to it is still 0 or 1 with overwhelming probability.

{35}------------------------------------------------

#### Step 1: showing that $E_1$ succeeds with overwhelming probability.

**Claim E.6.** For every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and good ( $\operatorname{st}_C$ ,  $\operatorname{com}$ ), Equation (E.10) holds for  $x_{\operatorname{com}}^* = (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  that is defined as follows: let  $\{(\operatorname{st}_0^\mu, \operatorname{i-msgs}_1^\mu)\}_{\mu \in [M]} = \{(x_1^\mu, \dots, x_{N_{lo}}^\mu)\}_{\mu \in [M]} \in (\{0, 1\}^{N_{lo}})^M$  be the good MPC initial state; then, let  $x_i^* := x_i^1 \oplus \cdots \oplus x_i^M$  for  $\forall i \in [n]$ .

<span id="page-35-1"></span>*Proof*. Fix any  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and good (st<sub>C</sub>, com), and let  $x_{\text{com}}^*$  be defined as in the claim statement. First, from the constructions of R.Dec<sub>1</sub> and  $E_1$ , the CNS of C.Prv<sub>1</sub>\*, and Equation (E.12), it follows that we have Equation (E.10) if we have

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{l} \forall \mu \in [M], \\ \mathsf{LD-Test.D}_{m_{10}|H|,3\zeta}(\mathsf{st}^{\mu},\pi^{*\mu;\mu}) = 1 \end{array} \right| \begin{array}{l} (Q^{\mu},\mathsf{st}^{\mu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{LD-Test.Q}_{D(X_{1,\mathrm{in}}^{\mu})} \text{ for } \mu \in [M] \\ (f,\{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C},\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq Q^{\mu} \text{ if } \mu = \nu \\ Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \text{ otherwise} \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.14}$$

Second, from the construction of R.Prv<sub>1</sub> and the CNS of C.Prv<sub>1</sub>\*, it follows that we indeed have Equation (E.14) due to Equation (E.9) (which is guaranteed to hold since ( $st_C$ , com) is good).

#### Step 2: showing that C.Prv<sub>1</sub> fails to prove false statement.

**Claim E.7.** For every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and good (st<sub>C</sub>, com), Equation (E.11) holds for  $x_{com}^*$  that is defined as in Claim E.6.

To prove this claim, we show the following claim.

<span id="page-35-3"></span>**Claim E.8.** For every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and good (st<sub>C</sub>, com), we have

<span id="page-35-4"></span><span id="page-35-0"></span>
$$\Pr\left[f(x_{COM}^*) = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \operatorname{st}_R) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Prv.Q}_1\\ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Prv}^*(\operatorname{st}_C, Q) \end{array} \right] \ge 1 - \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) , \tag{E.15}$$

<span id="page-35-2"></span>where  $x_{com}^* \in \{0, 1\}^n$  is defined as in Claim E.6.

Note that Claim E.8 implies Claim E.7 since Equations (E.15) implies Equation (E.11).

*Proof of Claim E.8.* We show three subclaims. Let P-SelfCorr be a parallel version of SelfCorr; see Algorithm 9.

## 

**Input:**  $\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$ .

- 1. Run  $(\tilde{Q}^{\mu:\nu}, \operatorname{st}_Q^{\mu:\nu}) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr.Q}_D(Q^{\mu:\nu})$  for each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .
- 2. Run  $(f, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \text{C.Prv}_1^*(\text{st}_C, \{\tilde{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}).$
- 3. Run  $A^{\mu:\nu} := \mathsf{SelfCorr}.\mathsf{Rec}_d(\mathsf{st}_O^{\mu:\nu}, \pi^{*\mu:\nu})$  for each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .
- 4. Output  $(f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$ .

**Sub-Claim E.1.** There exists a negligible function  $\epsilon_1$  such that for every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and every good (st<sub>C</sub>, com), we have

$$\Pr\left[ \mathsf{Correct}\left( \{S^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \right) \middle| \begin{array}{l} S^{\mu} \coloneqq \{s_{i}^{\mu}\}_{i \in [\log^{2} \lambda]} \ for \ \forall \mu \in [M], \ where \ s_{i}^{\mu} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{1,\mathsf{in},\mathsf{LDE}}^{\mu} \\ (f, \{A^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\mathbf{H}|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C}, \cdot)} (\{Q^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}), \\ where \ Q^{\mu : \nu} \coloneqq S^{\mu} \cup S^{\nu} \ for \ \forall \mu, \nu \in [M] \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \epsilon_{1}(\lambda) \ , \tag{E.16}$$

<span id="page-35-7"></span>where the event  $\mathsf{Correct}(\{S^\mu\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  is defined as follows. Let the correct view  $\{\mathsf{view}^\mu\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  be the views of the parties in the execution of  $\Pi$  on  $(f, \{(\mathsf{st}_0^\mu, \mathsf{i-msgs}_1^\mu)\}_{\mu\in[M]})$ , where  $\{(\mathsf{st}_0^\mu, \mathsf{i-msgs}_1^\mu)\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  is the good MPC initial states that is determined by  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com})$ . For  $\forall \mu, \nu \in [M]$ , let the correct assignment  $A_{\mathsf{corr}}^{\mu:\nu}$  (to the variables in  $\varphi_f^{\mu:\nu}$ ) be the assignment that is obtained from  $(\mathsf{view}^\mu, \mathsf{view}^\nu)$  as in Remark 3. Then,  $\mathsf{Correct}(\{S^\mu\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  is the event that  $A^{\mu:\nu}(s) = A_{\mathsf{corr}}^{\mu:\nu}(s)$  holds for  $\forall \mu, \nu \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\mu, \nu\}, \forall s \in S^\xi$ .

*Proof*. To show this subclaim, it suffices to show that there exists a negligible function  $\epsilon$  such that for every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and good ( $\mathsf{st}_C$ ,  $\mathsf{com}$ ), the following holds.

• For  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ ,  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{1,in}^{\xi}$ , we have

<span id="page-35-6"></span><span id="page-35-5"></span>
$$\Pr\left[A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \middle| \begin{array}{c} (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}), \\ \text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \text{ and } Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \epsilon(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.17}$$

{36}------------------------------------------------

(Indeed, given Equation (E.17), we can obtain Equation (E.16) for a negligible function  $\epsilon_1$  by using Claim D.7, the CNS of C.Prv<sub>1</sub>\*, and a union bound.) Now, we conclude the proof by noticing that for every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and every good (st<sub>C</sub>, com), the above follows from Lemma K.3 in Section K.1 (which guarantees that the values recovered from SelfCorr<sub> $m_{10}|H|,D(X_{1,in}^{\xi})$ </sub> and SelfCorr<sub> $m_{1}|H|,D(X)$ </sub> are equal) since  $\{(st_0^{\mu}, i\text{-msgs}_1^{\mu})\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  is the good MPC initial states.

**Sub-Claim E.2.** There exists a negligible function  $\epsilon_2$  such that for every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ , every good ( $\operatorname{st}_C$ ,  $\operatorname{com}$ ), and every  $\ell \in [N_{\operatorname{round}}]$ , we have

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c} \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{S^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right) \\ \land \neg \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right) \\ \land \neg \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right) \end{array}\right. \left. \begin{array}{c} S^{\mu}\coloneqq\{s_{i}^{\mu}\}_{i\in[\log^{2}\lambda]} \ for \ \forall \mu\in[M], \ where \ s_{i}^{\mu}\leftarrow I_{\ell,\mathsf{in},\mathsf{LDE}}^{\mu} \\ T^{\mu}\coloneqq\{t_{i}^{\mu}\}_{i\in[\log^{2}\lambda]} \ for \ \forall \mu\in[M], \ where \ t_{i}^{\mu}\leftarrow I_{\ell,\mathsf{out},\mathsf{LDE}}^{\mu} \\ (f,\{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})\leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C},\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}), \\ where \ Q^{\mu:\nu}\coloneqq S^{\mu}\cup S^{\nu}\cup T^{\mu}\cup T^{\nu} \ for \ \forall \mu,\nu\in[M] \end{array}\right] \leq N_{\mathsf{Aug}}\cdot\epsilon_{2}(\lambda) \ ,$$

where  $Correct(\{S^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  and  $Correct(\{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  are defined as in Sub-Claim E.1.

*Proof*. Since the prove phase of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  is just parallel executions of (PCP.P, PCP.V), this subclaim follows from Claim D.5.

**Sub-Claim E.3.** There exists a negligible function  $\epsilon_3$  such that for every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ , every good (st<sub>C</sub>, com), and every  $\ell \in \{2, ..., N_{\text{round}}\}$ , we have

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c} \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right) \\ \land \neg \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{S^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right) \\ \land \neg \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{S^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right) \end{array}\right. \left. \begin{array}{c} T^{\mu} \coloneqq \{t^{\mu}_{i}\}_{i\in[\log^{2}\lambda]} \, for \, \forall \mu \in [M], \, \, where \, t^{\mu}_{i} \leftarrow I^{\mu}_{\ell-1,\mathsf{out},\mathsf{LDE}} \\ S^{\mu} \coloneqq \{s^{\mu}_{i}\}_{i\in[\log^{2}\lambda]} \, for \, \forall \mu \in [M], \, \, where \, s^{\mu}_{i} \leftarrow I^{\mu}_{\ell,\mathsf{in},\mathsf{LDE}} \\ (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}^{*}_{1}(\mathsf{st}_{C},\cdot)} (\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}), \\ where \, Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq S^{\mu} \cup S^{\nu} \cup T^{\mu} \cup T^{\nu} \, for \, \forall \mu,\nu \in [M] \end{array}\right] \leq \epsilon_{3}(\lambda) \ ,$$

where  $Correct(\{S^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  and  $Correct(\{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  are defined as in Sub-Claim E.1.

*Proof*. As in the proof of Sub-Claim E.1, it suffices to show that there exists a negligible function  $\epsilon$  such that for every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ , every good (st<sub>C</sub>, com), and every  $\ell \in \{2, \ldots, N_{\text{round}}\}$ , the following holds.

• For  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ ,  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{\ell, in}^{\xi}$ , we have

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c} \operatorname{Correct}\left(\{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right) \\ \wedge A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^{*}) \neq A_{\operatorname{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^{*}) \end{array}\right. \left| \begin{array}{c} T^{\mu} \coloneqq \{t_{i}^{\mu}\}_{i\in[\log^{2}\lambda]} \text{ for } \forall \mu \in [M], \text{ where } t_{i}^{\mu} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\ell-1,\operatorname{out},\operatorname{LDE}}^{\mu} \\ (f,\{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \operatorname{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\boldsymbol{H}|,D(X)}^{\operatorname{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\operatorname{st}_{C},\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}), \\ \text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq T^{\mu} \cup T^{\nu} \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \text{ and } \\ Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^{*}\} \cup T^{\alpha} \cup T^{\beta} \end{array}\right] \leq \epsilon(\lambda) \ .$$

Fix any  $\lambda$ , (st<sub>C</sub>, com), and  $\ell$  as above, and for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ ,  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{\ell-1, \text{out}}^{\xi} \cup \mathcal{I}_{\ell, \text{in}}^{\xi}$ , let  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*)$  be the following probability.

$$p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \coloneqq \Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c} \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{T^\mu\}_{\mu \in [M]}\right) \\ \wedge A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A^{\alpha:\beta}_{\mathrm{corr}}(i^*) \end{array} \right. \left. \begin{array}{c} T^\mu \coloneqq \{t_i^\mu\}_{i \in [\log^2 \lambda]} \text{ for } \forall \mu \in [M], \text{ where } t_i^\mu \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\ell-1, \text{out}, \mathsf{LDE}}^\mu \\ (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\mathbf{H}|, D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq T^\mu \cup T^\nu \text{ for } \forall (\mu, \nu) \neq (\alpha, \beta) \text{ and } \\ Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \cup T^\alpha \cup T^\beta \end{array} \right]$$

In this notation, our goal is to show that we have  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \le \epsilon(\lambda)$  for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M], \forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}, \forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{\ell, \text{in}}^{\xi}$ .

First, we observe that we have  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M], \forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{\ell-1,\mathsf{out}}^{\xi}$ . Indeed, since the prove phase of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  is just parallel executions of (PCP.P, PCP.V), this bound follows from Claim D.6.

Next, we observe that we have  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M], \forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{\ell,\mathsf{in}}^{\xi}$  such that

- either  $i^* = (\xi, \ell, i)$  for some  $i \in [n_{st}]$ , i.e.,  $i^*$  is the index of a variable in  $\mathbf{w}_{\ell, \text{in}}^{\xi}$ , which corresponds to  $P^{\xi}$ 's internal state at the beginning of Round  $\ell$ ,
- or  $i^* \in \{(\alpha, \ell, n_{st} + \beta), (\beta, \ell, n_{st} + \alpha)\}$ , i.e.,  $i^*$  is the index of the variable  $\mathbf{w}_{\ell, \text{in}}^{\alpha}(n_{st} + \beta)$  or  $\mathbf{w}_{\ell, \text{in}}^{\beta}(n_{st} + \alpha)$ , where the former corresponds to  $P^{\alpha}$ 's incoming message from  $P^{\beta}$  in Round  $\ell$  and the latter corresponds to  $P^{\beta}$ 's incoming message from  $P^{\alpha}$  in Round  $\ell$ .

Fix any  $\alpha, \beta, \xi$  as above.

{37}------------------------------------------------

Case 1. When  $i^* = (\xi, \ell, i)$  for some  $i \in [n_{st}]$ , let  $j^* \in \mathcal{I}_{\ell-1, \text{out}}^{\xi}$  be the index of the variable  $\mathbf{w}_{\ell-1, \text{out}}^{\xi}(i)$ , i.e., the variable that corresponds to the i-th bit of  $P^{\xi}$ 's internal state at the end of Round  $\ell-1$ . Since P-SelfCorr $_{m|\mathbf{H}|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}$  is an adaptive local assignment generator (Claim D.4), we have

$$\Pr\left[A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*) \middle| \begin{array}{c} (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \mathsf{where} \ Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \ \mathsf{for} \ \forall (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \ \mathsf{and} \ Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*,j^*\} \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{E.18}$$

Hence, we have

$$\begin{split} p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \\ &\leq \Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c} \mathsf{Correct}\left(\{T^\mu\}_{\mu \in [M]}\right) \\ &\wedge A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A_{\mathsf{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \\ &\wedge A^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*) = A_{\mathsf{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*) \end{array} \right] \quad \begin{array}{c} T^\mu \coloneqq \{t_i^\mu\}_{i \in [\log^2 \lambda]} \text{ for } \forall \mu \in [M], \text{ where } t_i^\mu \leftarrow I_{\ell-1,\mathsf{out},\mathsf{LDE}}^\mu \\ &(f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ &\text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq T^\mu \cup T^\nu \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \text{ and } \\ &Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*,j^*\} \cup T^\alpha \cup T^\beta \end{array} \right] \\ &\leq p^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*) + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ , \end{split}$$

where in the last inequality, we use the fact that the event

<span id="page-37-0"></span>
$$\left(A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*)\right) \wedge \left(A^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*) = A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*)\right)$$

implies  $A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*)$  since we have  $A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*)$  from the definition of  $A_{\text{corr}}$ . Now, since we have  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(j^*) \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  from what is shown in the previous paragraph, we obtain  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  as desired.

Case 2. When  $i^* \in \{(\alpha, \ell, n_{\text{st}} + \beta), (\beta, \ell, n_{\text{st}} + \alpha)\}$ , let us focus on the case of  $i^* = (\alpha, \ell, n_{\text{st}} + \beta)$  for concreteness (the other case can be handled identically). Let  $j^* \in \mathcal{I}_{\ell-1,\text{out}}^{\xi}$  be the index of the variable  $w_{\ell-1,\text{out}}^{\beta}(n_{\text{st}} + \alpha)$ , i.e., the variable that corresponds to  $P^{\beta}$ 's outgoing message to  $P^{\alpha}$  in Round  $\ell-1$ . Since P-SelfCorr $_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\text{C.Prv}_1^*(\text{st}_C,\cdot)}$  is an adaptive local assignment generator, we have Equation (E.18). Hence, as in Case 1, we obtain  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \leq \text{negl}(\lambda)$  as desired.

Finally, we observe that we have  $p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ ,  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and  $\forall i^* \in I^{\xi}_{\ell,\mathsf{in}}$ . Fix any  $\alpha, \beta, \xi$  as above, and let us focus for concreteness on the case of  $\xi = \alpha$  (the case of  $\xi = \beta$  can be handled identically). Given what is shown in the previous paragraph, it remains to consider the case that  $i^* = (\alpha, \ell, n_{\mathsf{st}} + \gamma) \in I^{\alpha}_{\ell,\mathsf{in}}$  for some  $\gamma \in [M] \setminus \{\beta\}$ , i.e.,  $i^*$  is the index of the variable  $w^{\alpha}_{\ell,\mathsf{in}}(n_{\mathsf{st}} + \gamma)$ , which corresponds to  $P^{\alpha}$ 's incoming message from  $P^{\gamma}$  in Round  $\ell$ . Now, for  $\forall \gamma \in [M] \setminus \{\beta\}$ , what is shown in the previous paragraph implies that  $p^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*) \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Also, Claim E.5 and Lemma K.3 imply that

$$\Pr\begin{bmatrix} A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*) & (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\pmb{H}|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \notin \{(\alpha,\beta), (\alpha,\gamma)\}, \text{ and } \\ Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \in \{(\alpha,\beta), (\alpha,\gamma)\} \end{bmatrix} \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \enspace .$$

These two imply that

$$\begin{split} p^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \\ &\leq \Pr \begin{bmatrix} \operatorname{Correct}\left(\{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}\right) \\ &\wedge A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A_{\operatorname{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \\ &\wedge A^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*) = A_{\operatorname{corr}}^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*) \end{bmatrix} & T^{\mu} \coloneqq \{t_i^{\mu}\}_{i \in [\log^2 \lambda]} \text{ for } \forall \mu \in [M], \text{ where } t_i^{\mu} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\ell-1,\operatorname{out,LDE}}^{\mu} \\ &(f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \operatorname{P-SelfCorr}_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\operatorname{C.Prv}_1^*(\operatorname{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ &\text{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq T^{\mu} \cup T^{\nu} \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \notin \{(\alpha,\beta),(\alpha,\gamma)\} \text{ and } \\ &Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \cup T^{\mu} \cup T^{\nu} \text{ for } \forall (\mu,\nu) \in \{(\alpha,\beta),(\alpha,\gamma)\} \end{bmatrix} &+ p^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*) + \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) \\ &\leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) \end{aligned}$$

where in the last inequality, we use the fact that the event

$$\left(A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*)\right) \wedge \left(A^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*) = A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*)\right)$$

implies  $A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \neq A^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*)$  since we have  $A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\gamma}(i^*)$  from the definition of  $A_{\text{corr}}$ . This completes the proof of Sub-Claim E.3.

Now, we are ready to prove Claim E.8. Fix any  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and good (st<sub>C</sub>, com). For  $\forall \ell \in [N_{\text{round}}]$ , let  $p_{\text{in}}(\ell)$  be the following probability.

$$p_{\mathsf{in}}(\ell) \coloneqq \Pr \begin{bmatrix} \mathsf{Correct} \left( \{S^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \right) & S^{\mu} \coloneqq \{s_{i}^{\mu}\}_{i \in [\log^{2} \lambda]} \text{ for } \forall \mu \in [M], \text{ where } s_{i}^{\mu} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\ell,\mathsf{in},\mathsf{LDE}}^{\mu} \\ (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C},\cdot)} (\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \mathsf{where } Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq S^{\mu} \cup S^{\nu} \text{ for } \forall \mu,\nu \in [M] \end{bmatrix}$$

{38}------------------------------------------------

Similarly, for  $\forall \ell \in [N_{\text{round}}]$ , let  $p_{\text{out}}(\ell)$  be the following probability.

$$p_{\mathsf{out}}(\ell) \coloneqq \Pr \begin{bmatrix} \mathsf{Correct} \left( \{T^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \right) \middle| & T^{\mu} \coloneqq \{t_{i}^{\mu}\}_{i \in [\log^{2} \lambda]} \text{ for } \forall \mu \in [M], \text{ where } t_{i}^{\mu} \leftarrow \mathcal{I}_{\ell, \mathsf{out}, \mathsf{LDE}}^{\mu} \\ & (f, \{A^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\boldsymbol{H}|, D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_{1}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C}, \cdot)} (\{Q^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}), \\ & \text{where } Q^{\mu : \nu} \coloneqq T^{\mu} \cup T^{\nu} \text{ for } \forall \mu, \nu \in [M] \end{bmatrix}$$

From Sub-Claim E.2 and Sub-Claim E.3, we have

$$p_{\text{out}}(\ell) \ge p_{\text{in}}(\ell) - N_{\text{Aug}}\epsilon_2(\lambda) - \text{negl}(\lambda)$$

and

$$p_{\text{in}}(\ell) \ge p_{\text{out}}(\ell-1) - \epsilon_3(\lambda) - \text{negl}(\lambda)$$
.

Hence, we have

$$p_{\text{out}}(N_{\text{round}}) \ge p_{\text{in}}(1) - \text{negl}(\lambda).$$

Since we have  $p_{in}(1) \ge 1 - \text{negl}(\lambda)$  from Sub-Claim E.1, we have

$$p_{\text{out}}(N_{\text{round}}) \ge 1 - \text{negl}(\lambda)$$
.

Combining this with Claim D.6, for  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M], \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}, i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{N_{\text{round}}, \text{out}}^{\xi}$ , we have

$$\Pr \left[ A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = A_{\mathrm{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) \, \middle| \, \begin{array}{c} (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\boldsymbol{H}|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \mathsf{where} \,\, Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \,\, \mathsf{for} \,\, (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \,\, \mathsf{and} \,\, Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ .$$

Fix any  $\alpha, \beta \in [M], \xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , and let  $i^* \in \mathcal{I}_{N_{\text{round}}, \text{out}}^{\xi}$  be the index of the variable  $w_{N_{\text{round}}, \text{out}}^{\xi}(1)$ , which corresponds to the first bit of  $P^{\xi}$ 's internal state at the end of Round  $N_{\text{round}}$  (or equivalently the output of  $P^{\xi}$ ). Since P-SelfCorr $_{m|H|,D(X)}^{\text{C.Prv}_1^*(\text{st}_C, \cdot)}$  is an adaptive local assignment generator, we have

$$\Pr \left[ A^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = 1 \, \middle| \, \begin{array}{c} (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\boldsymbol{H}|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \mathsf{where} \,\, Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \,\, \mathsf{for} \,\, (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \,\, \mathsf{and} \,\, Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ \, .$$

Hence, from a union bound, we have

$$\Pr \left[ A_{\mathrm{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = 1 \, \middle| \, \begin{array}{c} (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\boldsymbol{H}|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \mathsf{where} \,\, Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \,\, \mathsf{for} \,\, (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \,\, \mathsf{and} \,\, Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ .$$

From the definition of  $A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}$  and the correctness of  $\Pi$ , we have  $A_{\text{corr}}^{\alpha:\beta}(i^*) = f(x_{\text{com}}^*)$ . Hence, we have

$$\Pr \left[ f(x_{\text{com}}^*) = 1 \, \middle| \, \begin{array}{c} (f, \{A^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{P-SelfCorr}_{m|\boldsymbol{H}|,D(X)}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \\ \mathsf{where} \,\, Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset \,\, \mathsf{for} \,\, (\mu,\nu) \neq (\alpha,\beta) \,\, \mathsf{and} \,\, Q^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \{i^*\} \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ .$$

Hence, from the "moreover" part of Claim D.4, we have

$$\Pr\bigg[f(x_{\text{\tiny COM}}^*) = 1 \ \middle| \ \begin{array}{c} (Q, \operatorname{st}_R) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Prv.Q}_1 \\ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Prv}^*(\operatorname{st}_C, Q) \end{array} \bigg] \geq 1 - \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$$

as desired. This completes the proof of Claim E.8.

This completes the proof of Lemma E.3.

*Remark* 6. By inspecting the proof of Claim E.6, one can easily see that Equation (E.10) holds even for a stronger version of R.Dec<sub>1</sub> that uses LD-Test.D<sub> $m_{10}|H|,\zeta$ </sub> in the verification instead of LD-Test.D<sub> $m_{10}|H|,3\zeta$ </sub>. (This observation is used later in the proof of Lemma G.2).

## <span id="page-38-1"></span>F Step 2: Non-WI Scheme with (1 - negl)-Soundness against CNS Provers

As the second step to our commit-and-prove protocol, we give a non-WI commit-and-prove protocol  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$  that is (1 - negl)-sound against (not necessarily well-behaving) CNS provers.

<span id="page-38-0"></span>In this step, we use a collision-resistant hash function family  $\mathcal{H}$ . For any  $hf \in \mathcal{H}$ , we denote by TreeHash<sub>hf</sub> an algorithm that computes the Merkle tree-hash of the input.

{39}------------------------------------------------

**Algorithm 10** Commit Phase and Open Phase of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ 

#### **Commit Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Com<sub>2</sub> sends a hash function  $hf \in \mathcal{H}$  to C.Com<sub>2</sub>.

<span id="page-39-2"></span>**Round 2:** Given  $(x_{\text{COM}}, \text{hf})$  as input,  $\text{C.Com}_2$  runs  $\{X_{1, \text{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \text{C.Com}_1(x_{\text{COM}})$ , and then outputs  $\{\text{rt}_{1, \text{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as the commitment and  $(\text{hf}, \{X_{1, \text{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  as the internal state.

......

#### **Open Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Dec.Q<sub>2</sub> works identically with R.Dec.Q<sub>1</sub>. That is, given i as input, R.Dec.Q<sub>2</sub> runs  $(\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \operatorname{st}_R) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Dec.Q}_1(i)$ , and then outputs  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as the query and  $\operatorname{st}_R$  as the internal state.

**Round 2:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  as input (where  $\operatorname{st}_C = (\operatorname{hf}, \{X_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$ ), C.Dec<sub>2</sub> defines  $\{\tilde{X}^{\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  just like C.Dec<sub>1</sub> does, and outputs  $\{\tilde{Y}^{\mu:\mu}|_{Q^{\mu}}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as the decommitment, where each  $\tilde{Y}^{\mu:\mu}$  is defined as

$$\tilde{Y}^{\mu:\mu}(z) \coloneqq \begin{cases} (\tilde{X}^{\mu:\mu}(z), \operatorname{cert}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}(z)) & \text{if } z \in D(X_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}) \\ (\tilde{X}^{\mu:\mu}(z), \bot) & \text{otherwise} \end{cases},$$

where for each  $z = (z_{\xi}, z_{\ell}, z_{\text{in}}, i) \in D(X_{\ell_{\text{in}}}^{\xi})$  (cf. Section D.2.2),  $\text{cert}_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}(z)$  is the certificate of Merkle tree-hash for revealing the i-th bit of  $X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$ .

**Verification:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, \{\tilde{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  as input, R.Dec.D<sub>2</sub> outputs

$$\tilde{x}_i \coloneqq \mathsf{R.Dec.D}_1\left(\mathsf{st}_R,\mathsf{com}',\left\{\mathsf{Filter}^{\mu}(\tilde{Y^*}^{\mu:\mu})\right\}_{\mu\in[M]}\right)$$

as the decommitted value, where  $com' = \varepsilon$  is an empty string, and Filter<sup> $\mu$ </sup> is the following function: given input of the form  $\{(x_z, cert_z)\}_{z\in Q}$ , it outputs  $\{\hat{x}_z\}_{z\in Q}$  such that  $\hat{x}_z := x_z$  if  $cert_z$  is a valid certificate w.r.t.  $(rt_{1,in}^{\mu}, z, x_z)$  and  $\hat{x}_z := \bot$  otherwise.

#### **F.1** Protocol Description

The formal description of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$  is given in Algorithm 10 and Algorithm 11.

#### <span id="page-39-0"></span>**F.2** Proof of Binding

**Lemma F.1.** Let  $\epsilon$  be any negligible function,  $\kappa_{\text{dec}}$  be the polynomial that is given in Lemma E.1, and  $C_2^* = (\text{C.Com}_2^*, \text{C.Dec}_2^*)$  be any  $\kappa_{\text{dec}}$ -CNS cheating committer-decommitter against  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ . Then, for every  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the following binding condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_2^*, \text{R.Com}_2 \rangle$ .

<span id="page-39-3"></span><span id="page-39-1"></span>• **Binding Condition:** If it holds

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c} \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M], \\ \beta_b^{\mu} = 1 \end{array} \right. \left. \begin{array}{c} (Q_b^{\mu}, \mathsf{st}_b^{\mu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{LD-Test.Q}_{D(X_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu})} \textit{for} \ \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \{\tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu : \mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Dec}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{Q_b^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}) \\ \beta_b^{\mu} \coloneqq \mathsf{LD-Test.D}_{m_{io}|\pmb{H}|, 3\zeta}(\mathsf{st}_b^{\mu}, \mathsf{Filter}^{\mu}(\tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu : \mu})) \\ \textit{for} \ \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \epsilon(\lambda) \ ,$$

then for every  $i \in [n]$  it holds  $\Pr[b_{BAD} = 1] \leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$  in the following probabilistic experiment  $Exp_2^{\operatorname{bind}}(\mathsf{C.Dec}_2^*, \mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}, i).$ 

- 1. For each  $\forall b \in \{0, 1\}$ , sample  $\{Q_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  by  $(\{Q_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \mathsf{st}_b) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Dec.Q}_2(i)$ .
- 2.  $Run\{\tilde{Y}_{b}^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}\leftarrow C.Dec_{2}^{*}(st_{C},\{Q_{b}^{\mu}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}).$
- 3. Let  $b_{\text{BAD}} \coloneqq 1$  if and only if  $x_0^* \neq \bot \land x_1^* \neq \bot \land x_0^* \neq x_1^*$  holds, where  $x_b^* \coloneqq \text{R.Dec.D}_2(\mathsf{st}_b, \mathsf{com}, \{\tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  for each  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ .

*Proof*. Fix any  $\epsilon$  and  $C_2^* = (C.Com_2^*, C.Dec_2^*)$  as above, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the binding condition does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of (st<sub>C</sub>, com) ← ⟨C.Com\_2^\*, R.Com\_2⟩.

To obtain a contradiction with the binding property of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  (Lemma E.1), we consider the following cheating committer-decommitter  $C_1^* = (\mathsf{C.Com}_1^*, \mathsf{C.Dec}_1^*)$  against  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$ .

- Committer. C.Com<sub>1</sub>\* runs ( $\operatorname{st}_C$ ,  $\operatorname{com}$ )  $\leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_2^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_2 \rangle$  internally, sends an empty string to  $\operatorname{R.Com}_1$  as the commitment, and stores ( $\operatorname{com}$ ,  $\operatorname{st}_C$ ) as the internal state.
- **Decommitter.** Given  $(\text{com}, \text{st}_C)$  and  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as input,  $\text{C.Dec}_1^* \text{ runs } \{\tilde{Y}^{*}^{\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \text{C.Dec}_2^*(\text{st}_C, \{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  internally, and sends  $\{\text{Filter}^{\mu}(\tilde{Y}^{*}^{\mu:\mu})\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  to  $\text{R.Dec}_1$  as the decommitment, where the function  $\text{Filter}^{\mu}(\tilde{Y}^{*}^{\mu:\mu})$  is defined as in  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ .

{40}------------------------------------------------

#### **Algorithm 11** Prove Phase of $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$

#### **Prove Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Prv.Q<sub>2</sub> works identically with R.Prv.Q<sub>1</sub>. That is, R.Prv.Q<sub>2</sub> runs  $(\{Q^{\mu,\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \{\mathsf{st}_V^{\mu,\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_1$ , and outputs  $\{Q^{\mu,\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  as the query and  $\{\mathsf{st}_V^{\mu,\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  as the internal state.

<span id="page-40-0"></span>**Round 2:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_C, f, \{Q^{\mu,\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  as input, C.Prv<sub>2</sub> does the following.

- 1. Obtain  $\{\text{view}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  just like C.Prv<sub>1</sub> does.
- 2. Run  $(\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}, \mathsf{rt}^{\nu}, \pi^{\mu:\nu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{PCP.P'}(\mu, \nu, f, \mathsf{view}^{\mu}, \mathsf{view}^{\nu}, \mathsf{hf})$  for every  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ , where  $\mathsf{PCP.P'}$  is identical with  $\mathsf{PCP.P}$  except for the following.
  - A hash function hf is given as an additional input.
  - The hash of  $X^{\mu}$  and  $X^{\nu}$ , denoted by  $\mathsf{rt}^{\mu} \coloneqq \mathsf{TreeHash}_{\mathsf{hf}}(X^{\mu})$  and  $\mathsf{rt}^{\nu} \coloneqq \mathsf{TreeHash}_{\mathsf{hf}}(X^{\nu})$ , are computed as additional outputs.
  - The proof  $\pi^{\mu:\nu}$  given by PCP.P' is  $\pi^{\mu:\nu} = (Y^{\mu:\nu}, \ldots)$  instead of  $\pi^{\mu:\nu} = (X^{\mu:\nu}, \ldots)$ , where  $Y^{\mu:\nu}$  is defined as

$$Y^{\mu:\nu}(z) \coloneqq \begin{cases} (X^{\mu:\nu}(z), \mathsf{cert}^\xi_{1,\mathsf{in}}(z)) & \text{if } \exists \xi \in \{\mu,\nu\} \text{ s.t. } z \in D(X^\xi_{1,\mathsf{in}}) \\ (X^{\mu:\nu}(z), \mathsf{cert}^\xi(z)) & \text{if } \exists \xi \in \{\mu,\nu\} \text{ s.t. } z \in D(X^\xi) \setminus D(X^\xi_{1,\mathsf{in}}) \\ (X^{\mu:\nu}(z), \bot) & \text{otherwise} \end{cases},$$

where  $\operatorname{cert}_{1,\text{in}}^{\xi}(z)$  is defined as in the open phase, and  $\operatorname{cert}^{\xi}(z)$  is defined as follows: for each  $z=(z_{\xi},i)\in D(X^{\xi})$  (cf. Section D.2.2),  $\operatorname{cert}^{\xi}(z)$  is the certificate of Merkle tree-hash for revealing the *i*-th bit of  $X^{\xi}$ .

3. Output  $(\{rt^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{\pi^{\mu:\nu}|_{Q^{\mu:\nu}}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  as the proof. (Note: the value of  $rt^{\mu}$  that is computed by PCP.P' $(\mu, \nu, ...)$  and the value of it that is computed by PCP.P' $(\mu, \xi, ...)$  are identical; see Remark 3.)

**Verification:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, f, \{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]})$  as input (where  $\operatorname{st}_R = \{\operatorname{st}_V^{\mu,\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}$  and  $\operatorname{com} = \{\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$ , R.Prv.D<sub>2</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $b^{\mu:\nu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PCP.D'}^{\geq \lambda \zeta}(\mathsf{st}_V^{\mu:\nu}, f', \mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}, \mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\nu}, \mathsf{rt}^{\nu}, \pi^{*\mu:\nu})$  for every  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ , where  $\mathsf{PCP.D'}$  is identical with  $\mathsf{PCP.D}$  except for the following.
  - The TreeHash<sub>hf</sub> roots  $rt_{1,in}^{\mu}$ ,  $rt_{1,in}^{\nu}$ ,  $rt^{\mu}$ ,  $rt^{\nu}$  are given as additional inputs.
  - Each test for  $X^{\mu:\nu}$  is made in the following manner.
    - (a) Make the query to  $Y^{\mu:\nu}$  instead of to  $X^{\mu:\nu}$ . Let  $\{(x_z, \mathsf{cert}_z)\}_{z\in Q}$  be the response from  $Y^{\mu:\nu}$ .
    - (b) Verify the test by considering  $\mathsf{Filter}^{\mu:\nu}(\{(x_z,\mathsf{cert}_z)\}_{z\in Q})$  to be the response from  $X^{\mu:\nu}$ , where  $\mathsf{Filter}^{\mu:\nu}$  is the following function: given input  $\{(x_z,\mathsf{cert}_z)\}_{z\in Q}$ , it outputs  $\{\hat{x}_z^{\mu:\nu}\}_{z\in Q}$  such that

$$\hat{x}_{z}^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \begin{cases} &\text{if } \exists \xi \in \{\mu, \nu\} \text{ s.t. } z \in D(X_{1, \mathsf{in}}^{\xi}) \text{ and } \mathsf{cert}_{z} \text{ is not a valid certificate} \\ &\text{w.r.t. } (\mathsf{rt}_{1, \mathsf{in}}^{\xi}, z, x_{z}), \\ &\text{or } \exists \xi \in \{\mu, \nu\} \text{ s.t. } z \in D(X^{\xi}) \setminus D(X_{1, \mathsf{in}}^{\xi}) \text{ and } \mathsf{cert}_{z} \text{ is not a valid} \\ &\text{certificate w.r.t. } (\mathsf{rt}^{\xi}, z, x_{z}) \\ &x_{z} & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

2. Output 1 if and only if  $b^{\mu:\nu} = 1$  for every  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .

{41}------------------------------------------------

In what follows, we observe that (1) the binding condition of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_1^*, R.Com_1 \rangle$ , and (2)  $C_1^*$  is well-behaving and CNS.

First, the binding condition of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com}) \leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_1^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_1 \rangle$  since  $C_1^*$  perfectly emulates  $(\operatorname{R.Com}_2, \operatorname{R.Dec}_2)$  for the internally emulated  $C_2^*$ .

Second,  $C_1^*$  is a well-behaving CNS committer-decommitter since (1) the CNS property of C.Dec<sub>1</sub>\* follows from that of C.Dec<sub>2</sub>\*, and (2) the consistency on  $D(X_{1,in}^{\mu})$  follows from the binding property of TreeHash<sub>hf</sub>.

Hence, we obtain a contradiction. □

#### **F.3** Proof of Soundness

<span id="page-41-0"></span>**Lemma F.2.** Let  $\epsilon_{SND}$  be any negligible function,  $\kappa_{prv}$  be the polynomial that is given in Lemma E.3,  $E_2$  be the extractor in Algorithm 12, and  $C_2^* = (C.Com_2^*, C.Prv_2^*)$  be any  $\kappa_{prv}$ -CNS cheating committer-prover against  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ . Then, for every  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the following soundness condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_2^*, R.Com_2 \rangle$ .

• Soundness Condition: If it holds

<span id="page-41-2"></span>
$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_2; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_2(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \ge 1 - \epsilon_{\scriptscriptstyle SND}(\lambda) \ , \tag{F.1}$$

then there exists  $x_{com}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that

$$\forall i \in [n], \Pr\left[x_i = x_i^* \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_2^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_2(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle\right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \tag{F.2}$$

and

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c|c} b = 1 & (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_2; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ \wedge f(x_{com}^*) = 0 & b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_2(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{F.3}$$

**Algorithm 12** Extractor  $E_2$  (against  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ )

**Input:** com, i, and  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\subset D(X^1_{1,\mathsf{in}})\times\cdots\times D(X^M_{1,\mathsf{in}})$ 

- <span id="page-41-1"></span>1. Run  $(f, \{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]})$ , where each  $Q^{\mu:\nu}$  is defined as  $Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq Q^{\mu}$  if  $\mu = \nu$  and  $Q^{\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \emptyset$  otherwise.
- 2. Output  $\{\tilde{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  as the decommitment, where  $\tilde{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}:=\pi^{*\mu:\mu}$ .

*Proof*. Fix any  $\epsilon_{\text{SND}}$  and  $C_2^* = (\text{C.Com}_2^*, \text{C.Prv}_2^*)$  as in the lemma statement, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the soundness condition does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_2^*, \text{R.Com}_2 \rangle$ .

To obtain a contradiction with the soundness of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  (Lemma E.3), we consider the following cheating committer-prover  $C_1^* = (\mathsf{C.Com}_1^*, \mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*)$  against  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$ .

- Committer. C.Com<sub>1</sub>\* runs ( $\operatorname{st}_C$ ,  $\operatorname{com}$ )  $\leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_2^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_2 \rangle$  internally, sends an empty string to R.Com<sub>1</sub> as the commitment, and stores ( $\operatorname{com}$ ,  $\operatorname{st}_C$ ) as the internal state.
- **Prover.** Given  $(\mathsf{com}, \mathsf{st}_C)$  and  $\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  as input,  $\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*$  first runs  $(f, \{\mathsf{rt}^\mu\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$   $\leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$ . For each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ , let  $\hat{\pi^*}^{\mu:\nu}: Q^{\mu:\nu} \to F \cup \{\bot\}$  be defined by

$$\forall z \in Q^{\mu:\nu} : \hat{\pi^{*}}^{\mu:\nu}(z) \coloneqq \begin{cases} \hat{x}_{z}^{\mu:\nu} & \text{if } z \in Q^{\mu:\nu} \cap D(X) \\ \pi^{*\mu:\nu}(z) & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

where  $\{\hat{x}_z^{\mu:\nu}\}_{z\in Q^{\mu:\nu}\cap D(X)}:= \mathsf{Filter}^{\mu:\nu}(\pi^{*\mu:\nu}|_{Q^{\mu:\nu}\cap D(X)})$  is defined as in  $\langle C_2,R_2\rangle$ . Then,  $\mathsf{C.Prv}_1^*$  sends  $(f,\{\hat{\pi^*}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  to  $\mathsf{R.Prv}_1$  as the proof.

In what follows, we observe that (1) the soundness condition of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_1^*, R.Com_1 \rangle$ , and (2)  $C_1^*$  is well-behaving CNS.

First, the soundness condition of  $\langle C_1, R_1 \rangle$  does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_1^*, \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Com}_1 \rangle$  since  $C_1^*$  perfectly emulates  $(\mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Com}_2, \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Dec}_2, \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Prv}_2)$  and  $E_2$  for the internally emulated  $C_2^*$ .

Second,  $C_1^*$  is a well-behaving committer-prover since (1) the CNS property of C.Prv<sub>1</sub>\* follows from that of C.Prv<sub>2</sub>\*, and (2) the consistencies on  $D(X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu})$  and on  $D(X^{\mu})$  follow from the binding property of TreeHash<sub>hf</sub>.

Hence, we obtain a contradiction.

{42}------------------------------------------------

Remark 7. Given the observation in Remark 6, one can easily see that Equation (F.2) holds even for a stronger version of R.Dec<sub>2</sub> that uses LD-Test.D<sub> $m_{10}|H|,\zeta$ </sub> in the verification instead of LD-Test.D<sub> $m_{10}|H|,3\zeta$ </sub>. (This observation is used later in the proof of Lemma G.2).

## <span id="page-42-4"></span>G Step 3: Non-WI Scheme with negl-Soundness against CNS Provers

As the third step to our commit-and-prove protocol, we give a non-WI commit-and-prove protocol  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$  that is negl-sound against CNS provers.

<span id="page-42-0"></span>In this step, we use a slightly extended version of the soundness amplification lemma of Brakerski et al. [BHK17], which is given as Lemma K.4 in Section K.2.

#### **G.1** Protocol Description

The formal description of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$  is given in Algorithm 13.

<span id="page-42-1"></span>**Algorithm 13** Commit Phase, Open Phase, and Prove Phase of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ 

#### **Commit Phase**

The commit phase of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$  is identical with that of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ .

.....

#### <span id="page-42-3"></span>**Open Phase**

The open phase of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$  is identical with that of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$  except that in the verification, R.Dec.D<sub>3</sub> uses LD-Test.D<sub> $m_{10}|H|,\zeta$ </sub> instead of LD-Test.D<sub> $m_{10}|H|,3\zeta$ </sub> for testing each  $\tilde{X}^{*\mu;\mu}$ .

.....

#### **Prove Phase**

The prove phase of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$  is identical with that of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$  except that in the verification, R.Prv.D<sub>3</sub> uses PCP.D'<sup> $\otimes \lambda$ </sup> instead of PCP.D' $^{\geq \lambda - \zeta}$  for verifying each proof  $\pi^{\mu:\nu}$ .

## **G.2** Proof of Binding

**Lemma G.1.** Let  $\kappa_v$  be the query complexity of (PCP.P, PCP.V),  $\kappa_{\text{dec}}$  be the polynomial that is given in Lemma E.1, and  $C_3^* = (\text{C.Com}_3^*, \text{C.Dec}_3^*)$  be any  $(\kappa_{\text{dec}} + \lambda \kappa_v)$ -CNS cheating committer-decommitter against  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ . Then, for every  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the following binding condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_3^*, \text{R.Com}_3 \rangle$ .

- <span id="page-42-2"></span>• Binding Condition: For every  $i \in [n]$ , it holds  $\Pr[b_{BAD} = 1] \leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$  in the following probabilistic experiment  $\operatorname{Exp}_3^{\operatorname{bind}}(\mathsf{C.Dec}_3^*, \operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com}, i)$ .
  - 1. For each  $\forall b \in \{0, 1\}$ , sample  $\{Q_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  by  $(\{Q_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \mathsf{st}_b) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Dec.Q}_3(i)$ .
  - 2.  $Run\{\tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}\leftarrow \mathsf{C.Dec}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\{Q_b^{\mu}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}).$
  - 3. Let  $b_{\text{BAD}} \coloneqq 1$  if and only if  $x_0^* \neq \bot \land x_1^* \neq \bot \land x_0^* \neq x_1^*$  holds, where  $x_b^* \coloneqq \text{R.Dec.D}_3(\text{st}_b, \text{com}, \{\tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu;\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  for each  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ .

*Proof*. Fix any  $C_3^* = (\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_3^*, \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_3^*)$  as above, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_3^*, \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Com}_3 \rangle$ , there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that we have  $\mathsf{Pr}[b_{\mathsf{BAD}} = 1] \geq 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  in the experiment  $\mathsf{Exp}_3^{\mathsf{bind}}(\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_3^*, \mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}, i)$ .

To obtain a contradiction, we first define a cheating committer-decommitter  $C_2^* = (\mathsf{C.Com}_2^*, \mathsf{C.Dec}_2^*)$  against  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$  by using  $C_3^*$ , and then show that  $C_2^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ .

Let us first give some preliminaries. First, from the definitions of R.Dec.Q<sub>3</sub> and R.Dec.D<sub>3</sub>, the probabilistic experiment  $\text{Exp}_3^{\text{bind}}(\text{C.Dec}^*, \text{st}_C, \text{com}, i)$  in the lemma statement can also be written as follows.

- 1. For  $\forall b \in \{0, 1\}$ , sample  $\{Q_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as follows.
  - (a) Run  $(Q_{b.0}^{\mu}, \mathsf{st}_{b.0}^{\mu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{LD}\text{-Test.Q}_{D(X_{1\,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu})}$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$ .
  - (b)  $\operatorname{Run}(Q_{b.1}^{\mu},\operatorname{st}_{b.1}^{\mu}) \leftarrow \operatorname{SelfCorr}(Q_{D(X_{1:n}^{\mu})}(\{(\mu,1,i)\}))$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$ .
  - (c) Let  $Q_b^{\mu} := Q_{b,0}^{\mu} \cup Q_{b,1}^{\mu}$ .
- 2. Run  $\{\tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}\leftarrow \mathsf{C.Dec}^*(\mathsf{st}_C,\{Q_b^\mu\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}).$ For each  $b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M],$  let  $\tilde{Y}_{b,0}^{*\mu:\mu}\coloneqq \tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu:\mu}|_{Q_{b,0}^\mu}$  and  $\tilde{Y}_{b,1}^{*\mu:\mu}\coloneqq \tilde{Y}_b^{*\mu:\mu}|_{Q_{b,1}^\mu}$
- 3. Let  $b_{\text{BAD}} := 1$  if and only if both of the following events hold.

{43}------------------------------------------------

- Event<sub>0</sub>: LD-Test.D<sub> $m_{10}$ </sub> $|H|,\zeta$ (st<sup> $\mu$ </sup><sub>b,0</sub>, Filter<sup> $\mu$ </sup>( $\tilde{Y}^{*\mu;\mu}_{b,0}$ )) = 1 holds for  $\forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]$ .
- Event<sub>1</sub>:  $x_0^* \neq \bot \land x_1^* \neq \bot \land x_0^* \neq x_1^*$  holds for  $x_0^*, x_1^*$  that are defined as follows.
  - (a) Let  $\tilde{x}_h^{\mu} := A_h^{\mu}(\mu, 1, i)$ , where  $A_h^{\mu} := \mathsf{SelfCorr.Rec}_{m_{10}|H|}(\mathsf{st}_{h,1}^{\mu}, \mathsf{Filter}^{\mu}(\tilde{Y}_{h,1}^{*\mu;\mu}))$ .
  - (b) Let  $x_b^* := \bot$  if  $\exists \mu \in [M]$  such that  $\tilde{x}_b^{\mu} \notin \{0, 1\}$ , and let  $x_b^* := \tilde{x}_b^1 \oplus \cdots \oplus \tilde{x}_b^M$  otherwise.

(Note that Event<sub>0</sub> depends only on  $\{\tilde{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}_{b,0}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}$  while Event<sub>1</sub> depends only on  $\{\tilde{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}_{b,1}\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}$ .)

Second, the probabilistic experiment  $\operatorname{Exp}_2^{\operatorname{bind}}(\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}^*,\mathsf{st}_C,\mathsf{com},i)$  in Lemma F.1 can be written similarly, where the only difference is that  $\operatorname{Event}_0$  is replaced with the following event.

• Event'<sub>0</sub>: LD-Test.D<sub> $m_0|H|,3\zeta$ </sub>(st'<sub>b,0</sub>, Filter<sup> $\mu$ </sup>( $\tilde{Y}^*_{b,0}^{\mu;\mu}$ )) = 1 holds for  $\forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]$ .

Now, we define  $C_2^* = (\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_2^*, \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_2^*)$ . Recall that we assume, for contradiction, that for infinitely many  $\lambda$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_3^*, \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Com}_3 \rangle$ , there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that we have  $\Pr[b_{\mathsf{BAD}} = 1] \geq 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  in  $\mathsf{Exp}_3^{\mathsf{bind}}(\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_3^*, \mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}, i)$ . Let us call such  $\lambda$ ,  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com})$ , and i be good. Then, the CNS of  $\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_3^*$  guarantees that there exists a constant  $c \in \mathbb{N}$  such that for every good  $\lambda$  and  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com})$ , we have

$$\Pr \Bigg[ \mathsf{Event}_0 \, \Bigg| \, \begin{array}{l} (Q^\mu_{b,0}, \mathsf{st}^\mu_{b,0}) \leftarrow \mathsf{LD\text{-}Test.} Q_{D(X^\mu_{1,\mathsf{in}})} \text{ for } \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \{\tilde{Y}^{*,\mu;\mu}_{b,0}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Dec}^*_3(\mathsf{st}_C, \{Q^\mu_{b,0}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}) \end{array} \Bigg] \geq \frac{1}{\lambda^c}$$

(where Event<sub>0</sub> is defined as in Exp<sub>3</sub><sup>bind</sup>). Hence, we can use Lemma K.4 (Soundness Amplification Lemma) to obtain a PPT oracle algorithm Amplify<sub>c</sub> such that for every good  $\lambda$  and (st<sub>C</sub>, com), we have

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{Event}_{0}^{\prime} \left| \begin{array}{l} (Q_{b,0}^{\mu},\mathsf{st}_{b,0}^{\mu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{LD-Test.Q}_{D(X_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu})} \text{ for } \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \{\tilde{Y}_{b,0}^{*}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathsf{Amplify}_{c}^{\mathsf{C.Dec}_{3}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C},\cdot)} (\{Q_{b,0}^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}) \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \right. \tag{G.1}$$

(where  $\mathsf{Event}_0'$  is defined as in  $\mathsf{Exp}_2^\mathsf{bind}$ ). Given  $\mathsf{Assign}_c$ , we define  $C_2^* = (\mathsf{C.Com}_2^*, \mathsf{C.Dec}_2^*)$  as follows.

- Committer. C.Com<sub>2</sub> works identically with C.Com<sub>3</sub>.
- **Decommitter.** Given  $\operatorname{st}_C$  and  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as input,  $\operatorname{C.Dec}_2^*$  works identically with  $\operatorname{Amplify}_c^{\operatorname{C.Dec}_3^*(\operatorname{st}_C, \cdot)}(\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$ .

Now, our goal is to show that  $C_2^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ . Since the CNS of  $C_2^*$  follows from Lemma K.4,<sup>33</sup> we focus on showing that for infinitely many  $\lambda$ , the binding condition of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$  in Lemma F.1 does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com}) \leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_2^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_2 \rangle$ . Toward this end, it suffices to show that for every good  $\lambda$  and  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$ , we have both

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{Event}_{0}' \middle| \begin{array}{l} (Q_{b}^{\mu}, \mathsf{st}_{b}^{\mu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{LD\text{-}Test.Q}_{D(X_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu})} \text{ for } \forall b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M] \\ \{\tilde{Y}_{b}^{*,\mu:\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Dec}_{2}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C}, \{Q_{b}^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}) \end{array}\right] \geq 1 - \epsilon(\lambda) \tag{G.2}$$

and  $\Pr[b_{BAD} = 1] \ge 1/\text{poly}(\lambda)$  in  $\exp^{\text{bind}}_2(\text{C.Dec}_2^*, \text{st}_C, \text{com}, i)$ . First, since  $\text{C.Dec}_2^*$  is identical with  $\text{Amplify}_c^{\text{C.Dec}_3^*}$  by definition, Equation (G.2) follows from Equation (G.1). Second, we obtain  $\Pr[b_{BAD} = 1] \ge 1/\text{poly}(\lambda)$  in  $\exp^{\text{bind}}_2(\text{C.Dec}_2^*, \text{st}_C, \text{com}, i)$  as follows.

• On the one hand, since we have

$$\Pr[\mathsf{Event}_1 \mid \mathsf{Event}_0] \ge \Pr[\mathsf{Event}_1 \land \mathsf{Event}_0] = \Pr[b_{\mathtt{BAD}} = 1] \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)}$$

in  $\operatorname{Exp}_3^{\operatorname{bind}}(\operatorname{C.Dec}_3^*,\operatorname{st}_C,\operatorname{com},i)$ , the "furthermore" part of Lemma K.4 guarantees that we have  $\operatorname{Pr}[\operatorname{Event}_1] \geq 1/\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  in  $\operatorname{Exp}_2^{\operatorname{bind}}(\operatorname{C.Dec}_2^*,\operatorname{st}_C,\operatorname{com},i)$ .

- On the other hand, Equation (G.2) and the CNS of C.Dec<sub>2</sub>\* guarantees that we have  $\Pr\left[\mathsf{Event}_0'\right] \geq 1 \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  in  $\mathsf{ExP}_2^{\mathsf{bind}}(\mathsf{C.Dec}_2^*, \mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}, i)$ .
- Hence, from a union bound, we have

$$\Pr[b_{\text{\tiny BAD}} = 1] = \Pr\Big[\mathsf{Event}_0' \land \mathsf{Event}_1\Big] \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)}$$

<span id="page-43-1"></span><span id="page-43-0"></span>

in  $Exp_2^{bind}(C.Dec_2^*, st_C, com, i)$  as desired.

This completes the proof of Lemma G.1.

<sup>&</sup>lt;sup>33</sup>We use  $\kappa_v$  as an upper bound on the query complexity of each test in LD-Test.

{44}------------------------------------------------

## **G.3** Proof of Soundness

<span id="page-44-0"></span>We first remark that, due to Lemma K.4 and the definition of C.Prv<sub>3</sub>\*, for every constant  $c \in \mathbb{N}$ , there is a PPT oracle algorithm Amplify<sub>c</sub> such that for every  $\kappa_{\text{max}}$ -CNS cheating prover  $C_3^* = (\text{C.Com}_3^*, \text{C.Prv}_3^*)$  and every  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_3^*, \text{R.Com}_3 \rangle$ , if it holds

$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_3; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_3(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \geq \frac{1}{\lambda^c}$$

for infinitely many  $\lambda$  (let  $\Lambda$  be the set of such  $\lambda$ ), then Amplify<sup>C.Prv\*\*</sup>(st<sub>C</sub>,·) is an adaptive ( $\kappa_{max} - \lambda \kappa_{v}$ )-CNS cheating prover such that there is a negligible function negl such that for every  $\lambda \in \Lambda$ ,

$$\Pr \left[ b = 1 \, \middle| \, \begin{array}{l} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_2; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{Amplify}_c^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_2(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ .$$

Now, as the soundness of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ , we prove the following lemma.

**Lemma G.2.** Let  $c \in \mathbb{N}$  be any constant,  $\kappa_v$  be the query complexity of (PCP.P, PCP.V),  $\kappa_{prv}$  be the polynomial that is given in Lemma E.3, and let  $E_3$  be the extractor in Algorithm 14. Then, for any  $(\kappa_{prv} + \lambda \kappa_v)$ -CNS cheating committer-prover  $C_3^* = (\text{C.Com}_3^*, \text{C.Prv}_3^*)$  against  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ , the following holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_3^*, \text{R.Com}_3 \rangle$ .

<span id="page-44-1"></span>• Soundness Condition: If it holds

$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_3; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_3(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \ge \frac{1}{\lambda^c} , \tag{G.3}$$
