then there exists  $x_{com}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that

$$\forall i \in [n], \Pr\left[x_i = x_i^* \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_3^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_3(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle\right] \ge 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \tag{G.4}$$

and

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c|c} b = 1 & (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_3; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ h \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_3(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{G.5}$$

#### **Algorithm 14** Extractor $E_3$ (against $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ )

**Input:** com, i, and  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \subset D(X^1_{1.\text{in}}) \times \cdots \times D(X^M_{1.\text{in}})$ 

- $1. \ \operatorname{Run} \ \{\tilde{Y}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \leftarrow E_2^{\operatorname{C.Prv}_2^*(\operatorname{st}_C, *)}(\operatorname{com}, i, \{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}), \ \text{where } \operatorname{C.Prv}_2^*(\operatorname{st}_C, \cdot) \coloneqq \operatorname{Amplify}_c^{\operatorname{C.Prv}_3^*(\operatorname{st}_C, \cdot)}(\cdot).$
- 2. Output  $\{\tilde{Y}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  as the decommitment.

*Proof*. Fix any c and  $C_3^* = (C.Com_3^*, C.Prv_3^*)$  as in the lemma statement, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the soundness condition does not hold with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow (C.Com_3^*, R.Com_3)$ . Let us say that any  $\lambda$  and  $(st_C, com)$  are good (for  $C_3^*$ ) if the soundness condition does not hold on  $\lambda$  and  $(st_C, com)$ . Then, from the binding property of  $(C_3, R_3)$ , it follows that for every good  $\lambda$  and  $(st_C, com)$ , we have Equation (G.3) and also have

• either there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that

<span id="page-44-3"></span><span id="page-44-2"></span>
$$\Pr\left[x_i = \bot \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_3^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_3(\mathsf{com}, i)\rangle\right] \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} , \tag{G.6}$$

• or there exists  $x_{\text{COM}}^* = (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that we have Equation (G.4), but we also have

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c|c}b=1\\ \land f(x_{\text{com}}^*)=0\end{array}\right|\begin{array}{c}(Q,\mathsf{st}_R)\leftarrow\mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_3;\ (f,\pi^*)\leftarrow\mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C,Q)\\ b\leftarrow\mathsf{R.Prv.D}_3(\mathsf{st}_R,\mathsf{com},f,\pi^*)\end{array}\right]\geq\frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)}\ . \tag{G.7}$$

To obtain a contradiction, we consider the following cheating committer-prover  $C_2^* = (C.Com_2^*, C.Prv_2^*)$  against  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ .

{45}------------------------------------------------

- C.Com<sub>2</sub>\* is identical with C.Com<sub>3</sub>\*.
- C.Prv<sub>2</sub>\*(st<sub>C</sub>, ·) is identical with Amplify<sub>C</sub>C.Prv<sub>3</sub>\*(st<sub>C</sub>,·)(·).

Note that, due to Lemma K.4,  $C_2^*$  is  $\kappa_{prv}$ -CNS.

We now show that  $C^*$  breaks the soundness property of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ . Fix any good  $\lambda$  and  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$ . First, since we have Equation (G.3), we have

$$\Pr \begin{bmatrix} b = 1 & (Q, \operatorname{st}_R) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Prv.Q}_2; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Prv}_2^*(\operatorname{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Prv.D}_2(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{bmatrix}$$

$$= \Pr \begin{bmatrix} b = 1 & (Q, \operatorname{st}_R) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Prv.Q}_2; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \operatorname{Amplify}_c^{\operatorname{C.Prv}_3^*(\operatorname{st}_C, \cdot)}(Q) \\ b \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Prv.D}_2(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{bmatrix}$$

$$\geq 1 - \operatorname{negl}(\lambda) \qquad (\operatorname{from Lemma K.4}) . \tag{G.8}$$

Next, consider the following two cases.

• Case 1. Assume that there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that we have Equation (G.6). Then, from the constructions of R.Dec<sub>3</sub>, C.Prv<sub>2</sub>\*,  $E_2$ , and  $E_3$ , we have

$$\begin{split} & \Pr\left[x_i = \bot \ \middle| \ (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_2^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_3(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle \right] \\ & = \Pr\left[x_i = \bot \ \middle| \ (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_3^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_3(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle \right] \\ & \geq \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} \end{split} .$$

This contradicts with the observation that is made in Remark 7.

• Case 2. Assume that there exists  $x_{\text{COM}}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that we have Equation (G.4), but we also have Equation (G.7). Then, from the furthermore part of Lemma K.4, we have

$$\begin{split} &\Pr\left[f(x_{\text{COM}}^*) = 0 \;\middle|\;\; (Q, \text{st}_R) \leftarrow \text{R.Prv.Q}_2;\; (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \text{C.Prv}_2^*(\text{st}_C, Q)\;\;\right] \\ &= \Pr\left[f(x_{\text{COM}}^*) = 0 \;\middle|\;\; (Q, \text{st}_R) \leftarrow \text{R.Prv.Q}_2;\; (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \text{Amplify}_c^{\text{C.Prv}_3^*(\text{st}_C, \cdot)}(Q)\;\;\right] \\ &= \Pr\left[f(x_{\text{COM}}^*) = 0 \;\middle|\;\; (Q, \text{st}_R) \leftarrow \text{R.Prv.Q}_3;\; (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \text{Amplify}_c^{\text{C.Prv}_3^*(\text{st}_C, \cdot)}(Q)\;\;\right] \\ &\geq \Pr\left[\begin{array}{c|c} b = 1 & (Q, \text{st}_R) \leftarrow \text{R.Prv.Q}_3;\; (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \text{C.Prv}_3^*(\text{st}_C, Q) \\ h \leftarrow \text{R.Prv.D}_3(\text{st}_R, \text{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array}\right] - \text{negl}(\lambda) \\ &\geq \frac{1}{\text{poly}(\lambda)} \quad \text{(from Equation (G.7))} \;\;. \end{split}$$

From a union bound with Equation (G.8), we obtain

$$\Pr \left[ b = 1 \land f(x_{\text{\tiny COM}}^*) = 0 \, \middle| \, \begin{array}{l} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Prv}.\mathsf{Q}_2 \\ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Prv}_2^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Prv}.\mathsf{D}_2(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \geq \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)}$$

and thus  $C_2^*$  breaks soundness of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ .

By combining what are shown above, we conclude that  $C_2^*$  breaks the soundness of  $\langle C_2, R_2 \rangle$ . By combining all the above, we obtain a contradiction. This concludes the proof of Lemma G.2.

## H Step 4: Non-WI Scheme with Standard negl-Soundness

<span id="page-45-0"></span>As the fourth step to our commit-and-prove protocol, we give a non-WI commit-and-prove protocol  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  that is negl-sound against (not necessarily CNS) provers. Additionally, we also show that  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  satisfies "2-privacy" in a similar sense to the MPC protocol  $\Pi$ . In this step, we use a 2-round PIR protocol PIR = (PIR.Enc, PIR.Res, PIR.Dec).

### **H.1** Preliminaries

<span id="page-45-1"></span>In  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ , we use PIR for the receiver to encrypt its PCP queries as in Kalai et al. [KRR14]. To simplify the exposition of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ , we introduce a triple of algorithms, (PIR.EncSet, PIR.ResSet, PIR.DecSet), that use PIR for this purpose. Let  $\kappa$  be a polynomial and  $Q \subseteq [N]$  be a subset of the indices of a database  $DB \in \Sigma^N$ .

{46}------------------------------------------------

- $(\mathbb{Q}, \mathsf{st}_{PIR}) \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{EncSet}_{\kappa(\lambda)}(1^{\lambda}, Q, N)$ :
  - 1. Choose a random injective function  $\tau: Q \to [\kappa(\lambda)]$ .
  - 2. For each  $i \in [\kappa(\lambda)]$ , run

$$(\mathbf{q}_i, \mathsf{st}^i_{\mathtt{PIR}}) \leftarrow \begin{cases} \mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{Enc}(1^\lambda, q, N) & \text{if } \exists q \in Q \text{ s.t. } \tau(q) = i \\ \mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{Enc}(1^\lambda, 1, N) & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

- 3. Output  $\mathbb{Q} := \{\mathbb{Q}_i\}_{i \in [\kappa(\lambda)]}$  and  $\mathsf{st}_{PIR} := \{\mathsf{st}_{PIR}^i\}_{i \in [\kappa(\lambda)]}$ .
- $\mathbb{X} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{ResSet}(1^{\lambda}, \mathbb{Q}, DB)$ 
  - 1. For each  $i \in [\kappa(\lambda)]$ , run  $z_i \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.Res}(1^{\lambda}, q_i, DB)$
  - 2. Output  $\mathbb{X} := \{\mathbb{X}_i\}_{i \in [\kappa(\lambda)]}$ .
- $X \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.DecSet}(\mathsf{st}_{\mathtt{PIR}}, \mathbb{X})$ 
  - 1. For each  $q \in Q$ , run  $x_{\tau(q)} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.Dec}(\mathsf{st}_{\mathtt{PIR}}^{\tau(q)}, \mathsf{x}_{\tau(q)})$ .
  - 2. Output  $X := \{x_{\tau(q)}\}_{q \in Q}$ .

## **H.2** Protocol Description

The formal description of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  is given in Algorithm 15, where polynomials  $\kappa'_{dec}, \kappa'_{prv}$  are defined as  $\kappa'_{dec} = \kappa_{dec} + \lambda \kappa_{v}$  and  $\kappa'_{prv} = \kappa_{prv} + \lambda \kappa_{v}$ , where  $\kappa_{dec}$  is the polynomial that is given in Lemma E.1,  $\kappa_{prv}$  is the polynomial that is given in Lemma E.3, and  $\kappa_{v}$  is the query complexity of (PCP.P, PCP.V).

The communication complexity of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  can be bounded by a polynomial in  $\kappa_{\text{dec}}$ ,  $\kappa_{\text{prv}}$ , and  $\kappa_{\text{v}}$ , all of which can be bounded by a polynomial in  $\lambda$  and log(Time(f)) (cf. Footnote 22, Footnote 24, Lemma D.2).

#### **H.3** Proof of Binding

**Lemma H.1.** Let  $C_4^* = (C.Com_4^*, C.Dec_4^*)$  be any PPT cheating committer-decommitter against  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ . Then, for every  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the following binding condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_4^*, R.Com_4 \rangle$ .

- Binding Condition: For every  $i \in [n]$ , it holds  $\Pr[b_{BAD} = 1] \leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$  in the following probabilistic experiment  $Exp_4^{\operatorname{bind}}(\mathsf{C.Dec}_4^*, \mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}, i)$ .
  - 1. For each  $\forall b \in \{0, 1\}$ , sample  $\{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  by  $(\{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \mathsf{st}_b) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Dec.Q}_4(i)$ .
  - 2.  $Run \{ \tilde{\mathbb{Y}}_b^{*\mu:\mu} \}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]} \leftarrow C. \mathsf{Dec}_4^* (\mathsf{st}_C, \{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}).$
  - 3. Let  $b_{BAD} := 1$  if and only if  $x_0^* \neq \bot \land x_1^* \neq \bot \land x_0^* \neq x_1^*$  holds, where  $x_b^* := \mathsf{R.Dec.D_4}(\mathsf{st}_b, \mathsf{com}, \{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}_b^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  for each  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ .

*Proof*. Fix any  $C_4^* = (\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_4^*, \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_4^*)$  as above, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_4^*, \mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Com}_4 \rangle$ , there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that we have  $\mathsf{Pr}[b_{\mathsf{BAD}} = 1] \geq 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  in the experiment  $\mathsf{Exp}_4^{\mathsf{bind}}(\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_4^*, \mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}, i)$ .

To obtain a contradiction, we define a cheating committer-decommitter  $C_3^* = (C.Com_3^*, C.Dec_3^*)$  against  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$  by using  $C_4^*$ , and show that  $C_3^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ . Specifically, consider the following  $C_3^* = (C.Com_3^*, C.Dec_3^*)$ .

- Committer: C.Com<sub>3</sub>\* is identical with C.Com<sub>4</sub>\*.
- **Decommitter:** Given  $\operatorname{st}_C$  and  $\{Q^{\mu}\}_{{\mu}\in[M]}$  as input,  $\operatorname{C.Dec}_3^*$  does the following.
  - 1. Run  $(\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}, \mathsf{st}^{\mu}_{\mathsf{PIR}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{EncSet}_{K_{\mathsf{dec}}}(Q^{\mu}, |\pi^{\mu:\nu}|)$  for each  $\mu \in [M]$ .
  - 2. Run  $\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu:\mu} \leftarrow \text{C.Dec}_{4}^{*}(\text{st}_{C}, {\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}})_{\mu \in [M]}).$
  - 3. Run  $\tilde{Y}^{*\mu:\mu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.DecSet}(\mathsf{st}^{\mu}_{\mathtt{PIR}}, \tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{*\mu:\mu})$  for each  $\mu \in [M]$ .
  - 4. Output  $\{\tilde{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  as the decommitment.

It is straightforward to see that for every  $\lambda$ , ( $\operatorname{st}_C$ ,  $\operatorname{com}$ ), and i such that we have  $\Pr[b_{\text{BAD}} = 1] \geq 1/\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  in the experiment  $\operatorname{Exp}_4^{\text{bind}}(\text{C.Dec}_4^*, \operatorname{st}_C)$ , we have  $\Pr[b_{\text{BAD}} = 1] \geq 1/\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  in the experiment  $\operatorname{Exp}_3^{\text{bind}}(\text{C.Dec}_3^*, \operatorname{st}_C)$ . (To see this, observe that  $\text{C.Dec}_3^*$  perfectly emulates  $\text{R.Dec}_4$  for the internally emulated  $\text{C.Dec}_4^*$ ). Furthermore, it is relatively easy to see that the security of PIR implies the CNS of  $\text{C.Dec}_4^*$ . (The proof of this fact is virtually the same as the proof of, e.g., [KRR13, Theorem 12] and [BHK16, Claim 7].) Hence,  $C_3^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ , and we obtain a contradiction.  $\square$ 

{47}------------------------------------------------

## <span id="page-47-0"></span>Algorithm 15 Commit Phase, Open Phase, and Prove Phase of $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$

#### **Commit Phase**

The commit phase of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  is identical with that of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ .

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

#### **Open Phase**

**Round 1:** Given i as input, R.Dec.Q<sub>4</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $(\{Q^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \mathsf{st}_R') \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Dec.Q}_3(i)$ .
- 2. Run  $(\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}, \operatorname{st}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{PIR}}) \leftarrow \operatorname{PIR.EncSet}_{\kappa'_{\operatorname{dec}}}(Q^{\mu}, |\pi^{\mu:\nu}|)$  for each  $\mu \in [M]$ . (Here,  $|\pi^{\mu:\nu}|$  denotes the length of the PCP proofs that are computed by the prover in the prove phase).
- 3. Output  $\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  as the query and  $(\mathsf{st}_R',\{\mathsf{st}_{\mathtt{PIR}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  as the internal state.

**Round 2:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_C, {\mathbb Q}^{\mu})_{\mu \in [M]}$  as input, C.Dec<sub>4</sub> does the following.

- 1. Define  $\tilde{Y}^{\mu:\mu}$  just like C.Dec<sub>3</sub> does.
- 2. Run  $\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu:\mu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.ResSet}(\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}, \tilde{Y}^{\mu:\mu})$  for each  $\mu \in [M]$ .
- 3. Output  $\{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  as the decommitment.

**Verification:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, \{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  as input (where  $\operatorname{st}_R = (\operatorname{st}_R', \{\operatorname{st}_{\operatorname{PIR}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$ ), R.Dec<sub>4</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $\tilde{Y}^{\mu:\mu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.DecSet}(\mathsf{st}^{\mu}_{\mathtt{PIR}}, \tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu:\mu})$  for each  $\mu \in [M]$ .
- 2. Output  $\tilde{x}_i := \mathsf{R.Dec.D}_3(\mathsf{st}_R',\mathsf{com},\{\tilde{Y}^{\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  as the decommitted value.

.....

#### **Prove Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Prv<sub>4</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $(\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]},\operatorname{st}_R')\leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_3.$
- $2. \ \operatorname{Run} \ (\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu},\operatorname{st}^{\mu:\nu}_{\operatorname{PIR}}) \leftarrow \operatorname{PIR.EncSet}_{\kappa'_{\operatorname{prv}}+\kappa'_{\operatorname{dec}}}(Q^{\mu:\nu},|\pi^{\mu:\nu}|) \ \text{for each} \ \mu,\nu \in [M].$
- 3. Output  $\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  as the query and  $(\mathsf{st}_R',\{\mathsf{st}_{\mathtt{PIR}}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  as the internal state.

**Round 2:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_C, f, {\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  as input, C.Prv<sub>4</sub> does the following.

- 1. Obtain  $\{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  and  $\{\pi^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  just like C.Prv<sub>3</sub> does.
- 2. Run  $\pi^{\mu:\nu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.ResSet}(\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}, \pi^{\mu:\nu})$  for each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .
- 3. Output  $(\{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{\mathbb{T}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  as the proof.

**Verification:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, f, \{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]})$  as input (where  $\operatorname{st}_R = (\operatorname{st}_R', \{\operatorname{st}_{\operatorname{PIR}}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]})$ ), R.Prv<sub>4</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $\pi^{*\mu:\nu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.DecSet}(\mathsf{st}^{\mu:\nu}_{\mathsf{PIR}}, \pi^{*\mu:\nu})$  for each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .
- 2. Run  $b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_3(\mathsf{st}_R',\mathsf{com},f,\{\mathsf{rt}^\mu\}_{\mu\in[M]},\{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$ . That is, do the following.
  - (a) Run  $b^{\mu:\nu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PCP.D'}^{\otimes \lambda}(\mathsf{st}_V^{\mu:\nu}, f', \mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}, \mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\nu}, \mathsf{rt}^{\mu}, \mathsf{rt}^{\nu}, \pi^{*\mu:\nu})$  for every  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$
  - (b) Let b := 1 if and only if  $b^{\mu:\nu} = 1$  for every  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .
- 3. Output *b*.

{48}------------------------------------------------

## **H.4** Proof of 2-Privacy

**Lemma H.2.** For any PPT cheating receiver  $R^*$ , there exists a PPT simulator  $S_4$  such that for  $\forall \lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,  $\forall x_{com} \in \{0, 1\}^n$  (where  $n = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ ),  $\forall \alpha, \beta \in [M]$ , and  $\forall z \in \{0, 1\}^*$ , the outputs of the following two experiments are identically distributed.

#### **Real Experiment:**

- 1.  $(\mathsf{hf}, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow R^*(x_{com}, z)$ .
- 2.  $\{\mathsf{rt}_{1 \text{ in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \mathsf{st}_{C}\} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Com}_{4}(x_{com}, \mathsf{hf}).$
- 3.  $(f, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \mathsf{St}_R') \leftarrow R^*(\mathsf{St}_R)$ . If  $f(x_{com}) \neq 1$ , the experiment aborts with output  $\perp$ .
- 4.  $(\{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{\mathbb{T}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Prv}_4(\mathsf{st}_C, f, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}).$
- 5. Output  $(st'_R, rt^{\alpha}_{1,in}, rt^{\beta}_{1,in}, rt^{\alpha}, rt^{\beta}, \pi^{\alpha:\beta})$ .

#### **Ideal Experiment:**

- 1. (hf, st<sub>R</sub>)  $\leftarrow R^*(x_{COM}, z)$ .
- 2.  $(f, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \mathsf{st}'_R) \leftarrow R^*(\mathsf{st}_R)$ . If  $f(x_{com}) \neq 1$ , the experiment aborts with output  $\perp$ .
- 3.  $(\mathsf{rt}_{1 \text{ in}}^{\alpha}, \mathsf{rt}_{1 \text{ in}}^{\beta}, \mathsf{rt}^{\alpha}, \mathsf{rt}^{\beta}, \pi^{\alpha:\beta}) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_4(\alpha, \beta, f, \mathsf{hf}, \mathbb{Q}^{\alpha:\beta}).$
- 4. Output  $(st'_R, rt^{\alpha}_{1,in}, rt^{\beta}_{1,in}, rt^{\alpha}, rt^{\beta}, \pi^{\alpha:\beta})$ .

*Proof*. First, we remark that from the constructions of C.Com<sub>4</sub> and C.Prv<sub>4</sub>, Step 2 and Step 4 of the real experiment can be written as follows.

- 2. Compute  $(\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]},\mathsf{st}_C)$ , where  $\mathsf{st}_C=(\mathsf{hf},\{X_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$ , as follows.
  - (a) Sample random  $x_{\text{MPC}}^1, \dots, x_{\text{MPC}}^M \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that  $x_{\text{MPC}}^1 \oplus \dots \oplus x_{\text{MPC}}^M = x_{\text{COM}}$ .
  - (b) Compute  $X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$  and  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$  as follows: sample random  $r_{\text{MPC}}^{\mu} \in \{0,1\}^{n_{\text{MPC}}}$ , let  $\mathsf{st}_0^{\mu} \coloneqq x_{\text{MPC}}^{\mu} \parallel r_{\text{MPC}}^{\mu}$ , let  $\mathsf{i-msgs}_1^{\mu} \coloneqq 0^M$ , let  $x_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu} \coloneqq \mathsf{st}_0^{\mu} \parallel \mathsf{i-msgs}_1^{\mu}$ , let  $X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$  be the low-degree extension of  $x_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu}$ , and let  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu} \coloneqq \mathsf{TreeHash}_{\mathsf{hf}}(X_{1,\text{in}}^{\mu})$ .
- 4. Compute  $(\{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{\mathbb{T}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  as follows.
  - (a) Run the MPC protocol  $\Pi$  on  $(f', \{st_0^{\mu}, i\text{-msgs}_1^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$ , and let  $\{view^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  be the view of the parties in this execution.
  - (b) Run  $(\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}, \mathsf{rt}^{\nu}, \pi^{\mu:\nu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{PCP.P'}(\mu, \nu, f', \mathsf{view}^{\mu}, \mathsf{view}^{\nu}, \mathsf{hf})$  for every  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .
  - (c) Run  $\pi^{\mu:\nu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.ResSet}(\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}, \pi^{\mu:\nu})$  for every  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .

Given the above description of the real experiment in mind, we consider the simulator  $S_4$  in Algorithm 16 (where we use the simulator  $S_{MPC}$  of  $\Pi$  that is guaranteed to exist due to its 2-privacy).

#### **Algorithm 16** Simulator $S_4$ (against $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ )

- 1. Run  $\{\text{view}^{\xi}\}_{\xi \in \{\alpha,\beta\}} \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_{\text{MPC}}(\{\alpha,\beta\},\{x_{\text{MPC}}^{\xi}\}_{\xi \in \{\alpha,\beta\}},1) \text{ for random } x_{\text{MPC}}^{\alpha},x_{\text{MPC}}^{\beta} \in \{0,1\}^{n}. \text{ Let } r_{\text{MPC}}^{\xi},\text{i-msgs}_{0}^{\xi} \text{ be the randomness and the dummy incoming messages of the first round that are recorded in view}^{\xi} \text{ for } \forall \xi \in \{\alpha,\beta\}.$
- <span id="page-48-0"></span>2. Compute  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\xi$  for  $\xi \in \{\alpha,\beta\}$  as follows: let  $x_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\xi \coloneqq x_{\mathsf{MPC}}^\xi \| \mathsf{r}_{\mathsf{MPC}}^\xi \| \mathsf{i}\text{-msgs}_1^\xi$ , let  $X_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\xi$  be the low-degree extension of  $x_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\xi$ , and let  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\xi \coloneqq \mathsf{TreeHash}_{\mathsf{hf}}(X_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\xi)$ .
- 3. Run  $(\mathsf{rt}^{\alpha}, \mathsf{rt}^{\beta}, \pi^{\alpha:\beta}) \leftarrow \mathsf{PCP.P'}(\alpha, \beta, f', \mathsf{view}^{\alpha}, \mathsf{view}^{\beta}, \mathsf{hf}).$
- 4. Run  $\pi^{\alpha:\beta} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{ResSet}(\mathbb{Q}^{\alpha:\beta}, \pi^{\alpha:\beta})$ .
- 5. Output  $(\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\alpha,\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\beta,\mathsf{rt}^\alpha,\mathsf{rt}^\beta,\mathsf{\pi}^{\alpha:\beta}).$

Now, it is easy to see that the output of the ideal experiment is identically distributed with that of the real experiment. □

49

{49}------------------------------------------------

#### **H.5** Proof of Soundness

**Lemma H.3.** Fix any constant  $c \in \mathbb{N}$ , and let  $E_4$  be the extractor in Algorithm 17. Then, for any PPT cheating committer-prover  $C_4^* = (C.Com_4^*, C.Prv_4^*)$  against  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ , the following condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_4^*, R.Com_4 \rangle$ .

• Soundness Condition: If it holds

$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q_4}; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D_4}(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \ge \frac{1}{\lambda^c} , \tag{H.1}$$

then there exists  $x_{com}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that

$$\forall i \in [n], \Pr\left[x_i = x_i^* \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_4^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_4(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle\right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \tag{H.2}$$

and

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c|c} b = 1 & (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q_4}; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ h \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D_4}(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \ . \tag{H.3}$$

#### **Algorithm 17** Extractor $E_4$ (against $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ )

**Input:** com, i, and  $\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$ .

- 1. Define  $\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  as follows: let  $\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\mu}:=\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}$  for  $\forall\mu\in[M]$ , and let  $\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}$  be sampled by  $(\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu},\mathsf{st}^{\mu:\nu}_{\scriptscriptstyle\mathrm{PIR}})\leftarrow\mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{EncSet}_{\kappa'_{\scriptscriptstyle\mathrm{dec}}}(\emptyset,|\pi^{\mu:\nu}|)$  for  $\forall\mu,\nu\in[M]$  such that  $\mu\neq\nu$ .
- 2. For each  $i \in [\lambda^{c+1}]$ , do the following.
  - (a) Run  $(\{\mathbb{Q}_i^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \mathsf{st}_i) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_4'$ , where  $\mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_4'$  is identical with  $\mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_4$  except that  $\mathsf{PIR.EncSet}_{\kappa'_{\mathsf{prv}}+\kappa'_{\mathsf{dec}}}$ .
  - (b) For each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ , choose a random permutation  $\tau : [\kappa'_{\text{prv}} + \kappa'_{\text{dec}}] \to [\kappa'_{\text{prv}} + \kappa'_{\text{dec}}]$  and define  $\mathbb{S}_i^{\mu:\nu} = \{s_j\}_{j \in [\kappa'_{\text{prv}} + \kappa'_{\text{dec}}]}$  as follows: parse  $\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}$  as  $\{\mathbb{Q}_j^{\mu:\nu}\}_{j \in [\kappa'_{\text{dec}}]}$  and parse  $\mathbb{Q}_i^{\mu:\nu}$  as  $\{\mathbb{Q}_{i,j}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{j \in [\kappa'_{\text{prv}}]}$ ; then, each  $s_j$  is defined as

$$s_j := \begin{cases} \mathbb{Q}_{i,k}^{\mu:\nu} & \text{if } k \coloneqq \tau^{-1}(j) \text{ satisfies } k \in \{1, \dots, \kappa'_{\text{prv}}\} \\ \mathbb{Q}_k^{\mu:\nu} & \text{if } k \coloneqq \tau^{-1}(j) \text{ satisfies } k \in \{\kappa'_{\text{prv}} + 1, \dots, \kappa'_{\text{prv}} + \kappa'_{\text{dec}}\} \end{cases}.$$

- (c) Run  $(f_i, \{\mathsf{rt}_i^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\rho_i^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{\mathbb{S}_i^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}), \text{ and parse each } \rho_i^{*\mu:\nu} \text{ as } \{\rho_{i,j}^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{j \in [\kappa_{\max}]}.$
- (d) For each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ , let  $\mathbb{Y}_i^{*\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \{ \mathbb{p}_{i,\tau(k)}^{*\mu:\nu} \}_{k \in \{\kappa'_{\text{prv}}+1,\dots,\kappa'_{\text{prv}}+\kappa'_{\text{dec}}\}}$  and  $\mathbb{T}_i^{*\mu:\nu} \coloneqq \{ \mathbb{p}_{i,\tau(k)}^{*\mu:\nu} \}_{k \in \{1,\dots,\kappa'_{\text{prv}}\}}$ .
- 3. Find the first  $i^* \in [\lambda^{c+1}]$  such that

R.Prv.D<sub>4</sub>(st<sub>i\*</sub>, com, 
$$f_{i*}$$
, {rt $_{i*}^{\mu}$ } $_{\mu \in [M]}$ , { $\pi_{i*}^{*\mu:\nu}$ } $_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}$ ) = 1.

If such  $i^*$  does not exist, output  $\perp$ . Otherwise, send  $\{\mathbb{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}_{i^*}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  to R.Dec<sub>4</sub>.

Remark 8 (Intuition of  $E_4$ ). Essentially,  $E_4$  emulates an execution of  $E_3$  while (1) inlining executions of Amplify<sub>c</sub> (Algorithm 22 in Section K.2) and  $E_2$ , and (2) encrypting the queries to the cheating prover by PIR.

*Proof*. Fix any c and  $C_4^* = (C.Com_4^*, C.Prv_4^*)$  as above, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of (st<sub>C</sub>, com) ← (C.Com<sub>4</sub>\*, R.Com<sub>4</sub>), the soundness condition does not hold.

To obtain a contradiction, we define a cheating committer-prover  $C_3^* = (\mathsf{C.Com}_3^*, \mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*)$  against  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$  by using  $C_4^*$ , and show that  $C_3^*$  breaks the soundness of  $\langle C_3, R_3 \rangle$ . Specifically, consider the following  $C_3^* = (\mathsf{C.Com}_3^*, \mathsf{C.Prv}_3^*)$ .

- Committer: C.Com<sub>3</sub>\* is identical with C.Com<sub>4</sub>\*.
- **Prover:** Given  $\operatorname{st}_C$  and  $\{Q^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  as input,  $\operatorname{C.Prv}_3^*$  does the following.
  - 1. Run  $(\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}, \mathsf{st}_{PIR}^{\mu:\nu}) \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR}.\mathsf{EncSet}_{\kappa'_{\mathsf{DIY}} + \kappa'_{\mathsf{dec}}}(Q^{\mu:\nu}, |\pi^{\mu:\nu}|)$  for each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .
  - 2. Run  $(f, \{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_{4}^{*}(\mathsf{st}_{C}, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}).$
  - 3. Run  $\pi^{*\mu:\nu} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.DecSet}(\mathsf{st}^{\mu:\nu}_{\mathsf{PIR}}, \pi^{*\mu:\nu})$  for each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ .

{50}------------------------------------------------

4. Output  $(f, \{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\pi^{*\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]})$  as the proof.

By carefully comparing  $E_4^{\text{C.Prv}_4^*(\text{st}_C,\cdot)}$  and  $E_3^{\text{C.Prv}_3^*(\text{st}_C,\cdot)}$ , one can see that for every  $\lambda$  and  $(\text{st}_C,\text{com})$  for which the soundness condition of  $\langle C_4,R_4\rangle$  does not hold against  $C_4^*$ , the soundness condition of  $\langle C_3,R_3\rangle$  does not hold against  $C_3^*$  either. (To see this, observe that the execution of  $E_4^{\text{C.Prv}_4^*(\text{st}_C,\cdot)}$  is perfectly emulated during the execution of  $E_3^{\text{C.Prv}_3^*(\text{st}_C,\cdot)}$ ). Furthermore, it is relatively easy to see that the security of PIR implies the CNS of C.Prv $_4^*$ . (The proof of this fact is virtually the same as the proof of, e.g., [KRR13, Theorem 12] and [BHK16, Claim 7].) Hence,  $C_3^*$  breaks the soundness of  $\langle C_3,R_3\rangle$ , and we obtain a contradiction.

## I Step 5: WI Scheme with Standard O(1)-Soundness

<span id="page-50-0"></span>Finally, we give our WI commit-and-prove protocol  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ . In this section, we use the following additional building blocks.

- Non-interactive statistically binding commitment scheme SBCom. (A non-interactive one is used for simplicity, and actually a 2-round one is sufficient. It is known that a 2-round statistically binding commitment scheme can be obtained from a one-way function, which in turn can be obtained from a collision-resistant hash function.)
- 2-round statistically hiding commitment scheme SHCom such that the first-round message from the receiver is a hash function. (Such a statistically hiding commitment scheme can be obtained from a collision-resistant hash function.)
- 2-round 1-out-of-M<sup>2</sup> OT protocol OT.

Also, we assume that all the building blocks (the above ones and the ones that are used in  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ ) are sub-exponentially secure, so that we can assume that (1) the committed value of a SBCom commitment can be extracted by brute force in a quasi-polynomial time  $T_{\text{SB}}$ , and (2) the security of SHCom, OT, and  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  holds against poly $(T_{\text{SB}})$ -time adversaries.

#### I.1 Protocol Description

The formal description of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  is given in Algorithm 18. It is easy to see that the communication complexity of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  is bounded by a polynomial in  $\lambda$  and the communication complexity of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ , and hence is bounded by a polynomial in  $\lambda$  and log(Time(f)).

## <span id="page-50-1"></span>I.2 Proof of Binding

**Lemma I.1.** Let  $C_5^* = (C.Com_5^*, C.Dec_5^*)$  be any poly( $T_{SB}$ )-time cheating committer-decommitter against  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ . Then, for every  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , the following binding condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5 \rangle$ .

- <span id="page-50-2"></span>• Binding Condition: For every  $i \in [n]$ , it holds  $\Pr[b_{BAD} = 1] \leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$  in the following probabilistic experiment  $Exp_5^{\operatorname{bind}}(\mathsf{C.Dec}_5^*, \mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}, i)$ .
  - 1. For each  $\forall b \in \{0, 1\}$ , sample  $\{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  by  $(\{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \mathsf{st}_b) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Dec.Q}_5(i)$ .
  - 2.  $Run \{ dec_b \}_{b \in \{0,1\}} \leftarrow C. Dec_5^*(st_C, \{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}).$
  - 3. Let  $b_{BAD} := 1$  if and only if  $x_0^* \neq \bot \land x_1^* \neq \bot \land x_0^* \neq x_1^*$  holds, where  $x_b^* := \mathsf{R.Dec.D}_5(\mathsf{st}_b, \mathsf{com}, \mathsf{dec}_b)$  for each  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ .

*Proof*. Fix any  $C_5^* = (\text{C.Com}_5^*, \text{C.Dec}_5^*)$  as above, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\text{st}_C, \text{com}) \leftarrow \langle \text{C.Com}_5^*, \text{R.Com}_5 \rangle$ , there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that we have  $\Pr[b_{\text{BAD}} = 1] \geq 1/\text{poly}(\lambda)$  in the experiment  $\text{Exp}_5^{\text{bind}}(\text{C.Dec}_5^*, \text{st}_C, \text{com}, i)$ .

To obtain a contradiction, we define a cheating committer-decommitter  $C_4^* = (\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_4^*, \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_4^*)$  against  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  by using  $C_5^*$ , and show that  $C_4^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ .

Concretely, we define  $C_4^* = (C.Com_4^*, C.Dec_4^*)$  as follows.

- Committer: Given hf as input, C.Com<sub>4</sub>\* does the following.
  - 1. Run (com', st'<sub>C</sub>)  $\leftarrow$  C.Com<sub>5</sub>\*(hf), and parse com' as {com<sub>sH</sub><sup>\(\mu\)</sup>} $_{\mu\in[M]}$ .
  - 2. Define com and  $st_C$  as follows.
    - (a) Sample  $\{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  by  $(\{\mathbb{Q}_b^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \mathsf{st}_b) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Dec.Q}_5(i)$  for  $\forall b \in \{0, 1\}$ .
    - (b) Run  $\{ \mathsf{dec}_b \}_{b \in \{0,1\}} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Dec}_5^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \{ \mathbb{Q}_b^\mu \}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}), \text{ and parse } \mathsf{dec}_0 \text{ as } (\{ \mathbb{\tilde{Y}}^*^{\mu : \mu} \}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{ \mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\mu, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sh}}^\mu \}_{\mu \in [M]}).$
    - (c) Let com :=  $\{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}_{1,\mathsf{in}}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  and  $\mathsf{st}_C \coloneqq (\mathsf{com},\mathsf{com}',\mathsf{st}_C')$  if  $\mathsf{dec}^{\mu}_{\mathsf{SH}}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\mathsf{com}^{\mu}_{\mathsf{SH}}$  to  $\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}_{1,\mathsf{in}}$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$ , and let  $\mathsf{com} \coloneqq \bot$  and  $\mathsf{st}_C \coloneqq \bot$  otherwise.

{51}------------------------------------------------

#### **Algorithm 18** Commit Phase, Open Phase, and Prove Phase of $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$

#### **Commit Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Com<sub>5</sub> works identically with R.Com<sub>4</sub>, that is, sends a hash function  $hf \in \mathcal{H}$  to C.Com<sub>5</sub>.

**Round 2:** Given  $(x_{COM}, hf)$  as input, C.Com<sub>5</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $(\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]},\mathsf{st}_C')\leftarrow\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_4(x_{\mathsf{COM}},\mathsf{hf}).$
- 2. Run  $com_{sh}^{\mu} \leftarrow SHCom_{hf}(rt_{1.in}^{\mu})$  for every  $\mu \in [M]$ . Let  $dec_{sh}^{\mu}$  be the decommitment for opening  $com_{sh}^{\mu}$  to  $rt_{1,in}^{\mu}$ .
- 3. Output  $\{com_{SH}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  as the commitment and  $(st_C', \{dec_{SH}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  as the internal state.

.....

#### **Open Phase**

**Round 1:** Given i as input, R.Dec.Q<sub>5</sub> runs  $(\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \operatorname{st}_R) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Dec.Q_4}(i)$ , and then outputs  $\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as the query and  $\operatorname{st}_R$  as the internal state.

**Round 2:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  as input (where  $\operatorname{st}_C = (\operatorname{st}'_C, \{\operatorname{dec}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$ ), C.Dec<sub>5</sub> runs  $\{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu : \mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Dec}_4(\operatorname{st}'_C, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  and then outputs  $(\{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu : \mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu}_{1, \mathsf{in}}, \operatorname{dec}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  as the decommitment.

**Verification:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, \{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{\mu^{\mu,\mu}}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu}_{1,\operatorname{in}}, \operatorname{dec}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  as input (where  $\operatorname{com} = \{\operatorname{com}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$ ), R.Dec.D<sub>5</sub> does the following.

- 1. Check that each  $\operatorname{dec}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\mu}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\mu}$  to  $\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}$ .
- 2. Output  $\tilde{x}_i := \mathsf{R.Dec.D_4}(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}', \{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{*^{\mu:\mu}}\}_{\mu \in [M]})$  as the decommitted value, where  $\mathsf{com}' := \{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}_{1,\mathsf{in}}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$ .

.....

#### **Prove Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Prv.Q<sub>5</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $(\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]},\mathsf{st}_R')\leftarrow\mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_4.$
- 2. Choose random  $\alpha, \beta \in [M]$ , and run  $(\mathsf{ot}_1, \mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{ot}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{OT}_1(1^{\lambda}, (\alpha, \beta))$ .
- 3. Output  $(\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \mathsf{ot}_1)$  as the query and  $(\mathsf{st}_R',\alpha,\beta,\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{OT}})$  as the internal state.

**Round 2:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_C, f, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \operatorname{ot}_1)$  as input (where  $\operatorname{st}_C = (\operatorname{st}'_C, \{\operatorname{dec}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$ ), C.Prv<sub>5</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $(\{\mathsf{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\mathsf{rr}^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Prv}_4(\mathsf{st}'_C, f, \{\mathsf{Q}^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}).$
- 2. Run  $com_{sB}^{\mu} \leftarrow SBCom(rt_{1,in}^{\mu} \| dec_{sH}^{\mu} \| rt^{\mu})$  for each  $\mu \in [M]$ . Let  $dec_{sB}^{\mu}$  be the decommitment for opening  $com_{sB}^{\mu}$  to  $rt_{1,in}^{\mu} \| dec_{sH}^{\mu} \| rt^{\mu}$ .
- 3. Run  $com_{sB}^{\mu:\nu} \leftarrow SBCom(\pi^{\mu:\nu})$  for each  $\mu, \nu \in [M]$ . Let  $dec_{sB}^{\mu:\nu}$  be the decommitment for opening  $com_{sB}^{\mu:\nu}$  to  $\pi^{\mu:\nu}$ .
- 4. Run ot<sub>2</sub>  $\leftarrow$  OT<sub>2</sub>(ot<sub>1</sub>, {msg}<sup> $\mu$ : $\nu$ </sup>}<sub> $\mu,\nu\in[M]$ </sub>), where msg $^{\mu:\nu}$   $\coloneqq$  (rt $^{\mu}_{1,\text{in}}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\mu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\nu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\nu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ , rt $^{\nu}$ , dec $^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}$ ).
- 5. Output  $(\{com_{SB}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{com_{SB}^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}, ot_2)$  as the proof.

**Verification** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_R, \operatorname{com}, f, \{\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{SB}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{SB}}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, \operatorname{ot}_2)$  as input (where  $\operatorname{st}_R = (\operatorname{st}_R', \alpha, \beta, \operatorname{st}_{\operatorname{OT}})$  and  $\operatorname{com} = \{\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$ ), R.Prv.D<sub>5</sub> does the following.

- 1. Run  $\mathsf{msg}^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq \mathsf{OT}_3(\mathsf{st}_{\mathsf{ot}},\mathsf{ot}_2), \text{ where } \mathsf{msg}^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq (\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\alpha,\mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sH}}^\alpha,\mathsf{rt}^\alpha,\mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sB}}^\alpha,\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\beta,\mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sH}}^\beta,\mathsf{rt}^\beta,\mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sB}}^\alpha,\mathsf{m}^{\alpha:\beta},\mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sB}}^{\alpha:\beta}).$
- 2. Check that
  - $\operatorname{dec}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\xi}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\xi}$  to  $\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\xi}$  for  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha,\beta\}$ ,
  - $\mathsf{dec}_{\mathtt{SB}}^{\xi}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\mathsf{com}_{\mathtt{SB}}^{\xi}$  to  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\xi} \| \mathsf{dec}_{\mathtt{SH}}^{\xi} \| \mathsf{rt}^{\xi}$  for  $\forall \xi \in \{\alpha,\beta\}$ , and
  - $dec_{sb}^{\alpha:\beta}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $com_{sb}^{\alpha:\beta}$  to  $\pi^{\alpha:\beta}$ .
- 3. Run  $\pi^{\alpha:\beta} \leftarrow \mathsf{PIR.DecSet}(\mathsf{st}^{\alpha:\beta}_{\mathsf{PIR}}, \pi^{\alpha:\beta})$ .
- 4. Output  $b^{\alpha:\beta} \leftarrow \mathsf{PCP.D'}^{\otimes \lambda}(\mathsf{st}_V^{\alpha:\beta}, f', \mathsf{rt}_{1.\mathsf{in}}^{\alpha}, \mathsf{rt}_{1.\mathsf{in}}^{\beta}, \mathsf{rt}^{\alpha}, \mathsf{rt}^{\beta}, \pi^{*\alpha:\beta})$ .

{52}------------------------------------------------

- 3. Output com as the commitment, and  $st_C$  as the internal state.
- **Decommitter:** Given  $\mathsf{st}_C$  and  $\{\mathbb{Q}^\mu_b\}_{b\in\{0,1\},\mu\in[M]}$  as input,  $\mathsf{C.Dec}_4^*$  aborts if  $\mathsf{st}_C=\bot$ , and does the following otherwise.
  - 1. Parse  $\operatorname{st}_C$  as  $(\operatorname{com}, \operatorname{com}', \operatorname{st}'_C)$ , and parse  $\operatorname{com}'$  as  $\{\operatorname{com}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$ .
  - 2. Run  $\{ \operatorname{dec}_{b}' \}_{b \in \{0,1\}} \leftarrow \operatorname{C.Dec}_{5}^{*}(\operatorname{st}_{C}', \{\mathbb{Q}_{b}^{\mu} \}_{b \in \{0,1\}, \mu \in [M]}).$
  - 3. For each  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , define  $dec_b$  as follows.
    - (a) Parse  $\text{dec}'_b$  as  $(\{\tilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{*}^{\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{\text{rt}'^{\mu}_{1 \text{ in}}, \text{dec}^{\mu}_{\text{SH}}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$ .
    - (b) Let  $\operatorname{dec}_b := \bot$  if (1)  $\operatorname{dec}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\mu}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\mu}$  to  $\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$  but (2)  $\{\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \neq \operatorname{com}$ . Let  $\operatorname{dec}_b := \{\widetilde{\mathbb{Y}}^{*^{\mu : \mu}}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  otherwise.
  - 4. Output  $\{ dec_b \}_{b \in \{0,1\}}$  as the decommitments.

Now, we show that  $C_4^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ . First, note that the binding property of SHCom implies that for  $\forall \lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com}) \leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_4^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_4 \rangle$ , we have that for  $\forall i \in [n]$ ,

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{st}_C \neq \bot \land (\exists b \in \{0,1\} \text{ s.t. } \mathsf{dec}_b = \bot)\right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$

in  $\operatorname{Exp}_4^{\operatorname{bind}}(\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_4^*,\operatorname{st}_C,\operatorname{\mathsf{com}},i)$ . Given this, one can easily see that from the assumption that  $C_5^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_5,R_5\rangle$ , it follows that for  $\forall \lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\operatorname{\mathsf{st}}_C,\operatorname{\mathsf{com}}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_4^*,\mathsf{R}.\mathsf{Com}_4\rangle$ , there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that we have  $\operatorname{Pr}[b_{\operatorname{BAD}}=1] \geq 1/\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  in the experiment  $\operatorname{Exp}_4^{\operatorname{bind}}(\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Dec}_4^*,\operatorname{\mathsf{st}}_C,\operatorname{\mathsf{com}},i)$ . Hence,  $C_4^*$  breaks the binding property of  $\langle C_4,R_4\rangle$ , and we obtain a contradiction.

## I.3 Proof of Witness Indistinguishability

**Lemma I.2.**  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  is witness indistinguishable.

<span id="page-52-2"></span><span id="page-52-0"></span>*Proof*. We show the witness indistinguishability by showing that there exists a super-polynomial-time simulator that can simulate the receiver's view in Experiment b (Definition 4) for  $\forall b \in \{0, 1\}$  without knowing the value of b. Fix any cheating receiver  $R^*$ , and consider the simulator  $S_5$  in Algorithm 19 (where we use the simulator  $S_4$  of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  that is guaranteed to exist due to its 2-privacy).

#### **Algorithm 19** Simulator $S_5$

**Commit Phase.** Given hf from  $R^*$ , do the following.

- 1. Simulate  $\{com_{SH}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  by committing to all-zero strings by using SHCom.
- <span id="page-52-1"></span>2. Send  $\{\operatorname{\mathsf{com}}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  to  $R^*$ .

**Prove Phase.** Given  $(f, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \mathsf{ot}_1)$  from  $R^*$ , does the following.

- 1. Extract the receiver's choice  $(\alpha, \beta)$  by  $(\alpha, \beta) := \mathsf{Ext}_{\mathsf{OT}}(\mathsf{ot}_1)$ . (Note: This step requires super-polynomial time; cf. Definition 13.)
- 2. Simulate  $com_{sB}^{\alpha}$ ,  $com_{sB}^{\beta}$ , and  $com_{sB}^{\alpha:\beta}$  as follows.
  - (a) Run  $(\mathsf{rt}_{1\,\mathsf{in}}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}_{1\,\mathsf{in}}^\beta, \mathsf{rt}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\beta, \pi^{\alpha:\beta}) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_4(\alpha, \beta, f, \mathsf{hf}, \mathbb{Q}^{\alpha:\beta}).$
  - (b) For each  $\xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , compute (by brute force) a decommitment  $\operatorname{dec}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\xi}$  for opening  $\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\xi}$  to  $\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\xi}$ .
  - (c) For each  $\xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , obtain  $\mathsf{com}_{\mathtt{SB}}^{\xi}$  by  $\mathsf{com}_{\mathtt{SB}}^{\xi} \leftarrow \mathsf{SBCom}(\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\xi} \| \mathsf{dec}_{\mathtt{SH}}^{\xi} \| \mathsf{rt}^{\xi})$ .
  - (d) Obtain  $com_{sB}^{\alpha:\beta}$  by  $com_{sB}^{\alpha:\beta} \leftarrow SBCom(\pi^{\alpha:\beta})$ .
- 3. Simulate  $com_{SB}^{\mu}$ ,  $com_{SB}^{\nu}$ , and  $com_{SB}^{\mu:\nu}$  for  $\forall (\mu, \nu) \neq (\alpha, \beta)$  by committing to all-zero strings by using SBCom.
- 4. Simulate ot<sub>2</sub> by ot<sub>2</sub>  $\leftarrow$  OT<sub>2</sub>(ot<sub>1</sub>, {msg<sup> $\mu$ : $\nu$ </sup>}<sub> $\mu,\nu\in[M]$ </sub>), where

$$\mathsf{msg}^{\alpha:\beta} \coloneqq (\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\alpha, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sH}}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\alpha, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sB}}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\beta, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sH}}^\beta, \mathsf{rt}^\beta, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sB}}^\beta, \pi^{\alpha:\beta}, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{sB}}^{\alpha:\beta}) \enspace ,$$

and  $\mathsf{msg}^{\mu:\nu}$  for  $\forall (\mu, \nu) \neq (\alpha, \beta)$  is an all-zero string.

5. Output  $(f, \{com_{sB}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{com_{sB}^{\mu : \nu}\}_{\mu, \nu \in [M]}, ot_2)$  as the proof.

Now, we consider a sequence of hybrid experiments.

{53}------------------------------------------------

- Hybrid  $H_0$  is identical with the real experiment.
- Hybrid  $H_1$  is identical with  $H_0$  except that in the prove phase, (1) the receiver's choice  $(\alpha, \beta)$  is extracted by  $(\alpha, \beta) := \text{Ext}_{OT}(\text{ot}_1)$ , and (2)  $\text{msg}^{\mu:\nu}$  for  $\forall (\mu, \nu) \neq (\alpha, \beta)$  is an all-zero string.
- Hybrid  $H_2$  is identical with  $H_1$  except that in the prove phase,  $com_{sB}^{\mu}$ ,  $com_{sB}^{\nu}$ , and  $com_{sB}^{\mu;\nu}$  for  $\forall (\mu, \nu) \neq (\alpha, \beta)$  are generated by committing to all-zero strings by using SBCom.
- Hybrid  $H_3$  is identical with  $H_2$  except that (1) in the commit phase,  $\{com_{sH}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  is generate by committing to all-zero strings by using SHCom, and (2) in the prove phase,  $com_{sB}^{\alpha}$  and  $com_{sB}^{\beta}$  are generated as follows.
  - 1. For each  $\xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , compute (by brute force) a decommitment  $\operatorname{dec}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\xi}$  for opening  $\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\mu}$  to  $\operatorname{rt}_{\operatorname{Lin}}^{\xi}$ .
  - 2. For each  $\xi \in \{\alpha, \beta\}$ , obtain  $\mathsf{com}_{\mathtt{SB}}^{\xi}$  by  $\mathsf{com}_{\mathtt{SB}}^{\xi} \leftarrow \mathsf{SBCom}(\mathsf{rt}_{\mathtt{lin}}^{\xi} \| \mathsf{dec}_{\mathtt{SH}}^{\xi} \| \mathsf{rt}^{\xi})$ .
- Hybrid  $H_4$  is identical with  $H_3$  except that  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\beta, \mathsf{and} \ \pi^{\alpha:\beta}$  are generated by  $(\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\beta, \mathsf{rt}^\alpha, \mathsf{rt}^\beta) \leftarrow \mathcal{S}_4(\alpha, \beta, f, \mathsf{hf}, \mathbb{Q}^{\alpha:\beta}).$
- Hybrid  $H_5$  is identical with the ideal execution.

From a hybrid argument, it suffices to show that the output of each hybrid is indistinguishable from that of the preceding one.

**Claim I.1.** The output of  $H_1$  is computationally indistinguishable from that of  $H_0$ .

<span id="page-53-1"></span>*Proof*. Assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda$ , the output of  $H_0$  and that of  $H_1$  are distinguishable. Fix any such  $\lambda$ . From an average argument, it follows that the output of  $H_0$  and that of  $H_1$  are distinguishable even when the transcript of their executions are fixed up until Round 1 of the prove phase. Since the transcript up until Round 1 of the prove phase determines the value of  $(\alpha, \beta)$ , and Round 2 of the prove phase of  $H_1$  can be emulated in polynomial time given  $(\alpha, \beta)$ , we can now break the sender security of OT, and hence obtain a contradiction.

**Claim I.2.** The output of  $H_2$  is computationally indistinguishable from that of  $H_1$ .

*Proof*. This claim can be proven similarly to Claim I.1; the difference is that we rely on the hiding property of SBCom instead of the sender security of OT.

**Claim I.3.** The output of  $H_3$  is statistically indistinguishable from that of  $H_2$ .

*Proof*. This claim follows from the statistical hiding property of SHCom.

**Claim I.4.** The output of  $H_4$  is identically distributed with that of  $H_3$ .

*Proof*. This claim follows from the 2-privacy of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ .

**Claim I.5.** The output of  $H_5$  is identically distributed with that of  $H_4$ .

*Proof*. This claim can be proven trivially since, by inspection, one can see that the messages that are sent to  $R^*$  in  $H_4$  are generated identically with those in the ideal execution.

This concludes the proof of Lemma I.2.

## I.4 Proof of Soundness

**Lemma I.3.** Fix any constant  $c \in \mathbb{N}$ , and let  $E_5$  be the extractor in Algorithm 20. Then, for any poly( $T_{SB}$ )-time cheating committer-prover  $C_5^* = (C.Com_5^*, C.Prv_5^*)$  against  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ , the following condition holds with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5 \rangle$ .

<span id="page-53-4"></span><span id="page-53-0"></span>• Soundness Condition: If it holds

$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_5; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_5^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_5(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \ge 1 - \frac{1}{M^2} + \frac{1}{\lambda^c} \ , \tag{I.1}$$

<span id="page-53-3"></span><span id="page-53-2"></span>

then there exists  $x_{com}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that

$$\forall i \in [n], \Pr\left[x_i = x_i^* \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_5^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_5^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_5(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle\right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda) \tag{I.2}$$

and

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c|c}b=1\\ \land f(x_{com}^*)=0\end{array}\right|\begin{array}{c}(Q,\operatorname{st}_R)\leftarrow\operatorname{R.Prv.Q}_5;\ (f,\pi^*)\leftarrow\operatorname{C.Prv}_5^*(\operatorname{st}_C,Q)\\ b\leftarrow\operatorname{R.Prv.D}_5(\operatorname{st}_R,\operatorname{com},f,\pi^*)\end{array}\right]\leq 1-\frac{1}{M^2}+\operatorname{negl}(\lambda)\ .$$

{54}------------------------------------------------

#### <span id="page-54-0"></span>**Algorithm 20** Extractor $E_5$ (against $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ )

**Input:** com, i, and  $\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$ , where com =  $\{\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{SH}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$ .

- **Step 1.** Repeat the following at most  $T_{\text{SB}}$  times to obtain  $\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}, \mathsf{dec}_{\text{SH}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  such that each  $\mathsf{dec}_{\text{SH}}^{\mu}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\mathsf{com}_{\text{SH}}^{\mu}$  to  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}$ .
  - 1. Run  $(\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]},\mathsf{ot}_1,\mathsf{st}_R)\leftarrow\mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_5.$
  - 2. Run  $(f, \{com_{sb}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{com_{sb}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_2) \leftarrow C.Prv_5^*(st_C, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_1).$
  - 3. Extract the committed values of  $\{com_{sB}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  by brute force. Let  $\{rt_{1,in}^{\mu}\|dec_{sH}^{\mu}\|rt^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$  be the extracted values.

Abort if such  $\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathtt{SH}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  does not obtained after repeating the above for  $T_{\mathtt{SB}}$  times.

- Step 2. Run  $\{\mathbb{Y}^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}\leftarrow E_4^{\mathcal{A}}(\mathsf{com}',i,\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$ , where  $\mathsf{com}'$  is defined as  $\mathsf{com}'\coloneqq\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}$ , and  $\mathcal{A}$  is the cheating prover that works as follows on input any  $\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$ :
  - 1. Run  $(f, \{com_{s_B}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{com_{s_B}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_2) \leftarrow C.Prv_5^*(st_C, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_1)$ , where ot\_1 is sampled by  $(ot_1, st_{ot}) \leftarrow OT_1(1^{\lambda}, (\alpha, \beta))$  for random  $\alpha, \beta \in [M]$ .
  - 2. Define proof as follows.
    - (a) Extract the committed values of  $\{com_{s_B}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{com_{s_B}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  by brute force. Let  $\{rt_{1,in}^{\mu} \parallel dec_{s_H}^{\mu} \parallel rt^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{m^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  be the extracted values.
    - (b) Let proof :=  $\bot$  if (1)  $\operatorname{dec}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\mu}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\mu}$  to  $\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$  but (2)  $\{\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  is not equal to the one that is obtained in Step 1. Let proof :=  $(\{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]})$  otherwise.
  - 3. Output (f, proof) as the proof.

**Step 3.** Send  $(\{Y^{*\mu:\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}, \mathsf{dec}_{\mathsf{SH}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]})$  to R.Dec<sub>5</sub>.

*Proof*. Fix any c and  $C_5^* = (C.Com_5^*, C.Prv_5^*)$  as above, and assume for contradiction that for infinitely many  $\lambda$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow (C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5)$ , the soundness condition does not hold.

To obtain a contradiction, we define a cheating committer-prover  $C_4^* = (\mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Com}_4^*, \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Prv}_4^*)$  against  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$  by using  $C_5^*$ , and show that  $C_4^*$  breaks the soundness of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ .

Concretely, we consider the following  $C_4^* = (C.Com_4^*, C.Prv_4^*)$ .

- Committer: Given hf as input, C.Com<sub>4</sub> does the following.
  - 1. Run (com', st'<sub>C</sub>)  $\leftarrow$  C.Com<sub>5</sub>\*(hf), and parse com' as {com<sub>SH</sub>}<sub> $\mu \in [M]$ </sub>.
  - 2. Repeat the following at most  $T_{\text{SB}}$  times to obtain  $\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}, \mathsf{dec}_{\text{SH}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  such that each  $\mathsf{dec}_{\text{SH}}^{\mu}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\mathsf{com}_{\text{SH}}^{\mu}$  to  $\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}$ .
    - (a) Run  $(\{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}, \mathsf{ot}_1, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_5$ .
    - (b) Run  $(f, \{com_{s_B}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{com_{s_B}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_2) \leftarrow C.Prv_5^*(st_C, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_1).$
    - (c) Extract the committed values of  $\{com_{SB}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  by brute force. Let  $\{rt_{1,in}^{\mu} \| dec_{SH}^{\mu} \| rt^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  be the extracted values.

Let  $b_{\text{BAD}} := 1$  if such  $\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}, \mathsf{dec}_{\text{SH}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  does not obtained after repeating the above  $T_{\text{SB}}$  times, and let  $b_{\text{BAD}} := 0$  otherwise.

- 3. If  $b_{\text{BAD}} = 0$ , output com :=  $\{\mathsf{rt}_{1,\mathsf{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  as the commitment and  $\mathsf{st}_C := (\mathsf{com}, \mathsf{com}', \mathsf{st}_C')$  as the internal state. If  $b_{\text{BAD}} = 1$ , output com :=  $\bot$  as the commitment and  $\mathsf{st}_C := (\bot, \mathsf{com}', \mathsf{st}_C')$  as the internal state.
- **Prover:** Given  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]})$  as input, C.Prv<sub>4</sub> does the following.
  - 1. Parse  $\operatorname{st}_C$  as  $(\operatorname{com}, \operatorname{com}', \operatorname{st}'_C)$ , and parse  $\operatorname{com}'$  as  $\{\operatorname{com}^{\mu}_{\operatorname{SH}}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$ . Abort if  $\operatorname{com} = \bot$ .
  - 2. Run  $(f, \{com_{s_B}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{com_{s_B}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_2) \leftarrow C.Prv_5^*(st_C', \{\mathbb{Q}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]}, ot_1)$ , where ot\_1 is sampled by  $(ot_1, st_{ot}) \leftarrow OT_1(1^{\lambda}, (\alpha, \beta))$  for random  $\alpha, \beta \in [M]$ .
  - 3. Define proof as follows.
    - (a) Extract the committed values of  $\{com_{sB}^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{com_{sB}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  by brute force. Let  $\{rt_{1,in}^{\mu} \parallel dec_{sH}^{\mu} \parallel rt^{\mu}\}_{\mu\in[M]}, \{m^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu\in[M]}$  be the extracted values.
    - (b) Let proof :=  $\bot$  if (1)  $\operatorname{dec}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\mu}$  is a valid decommitment for opening  $\operatorname{com}_{\operatorname{sh}}^{\mu}$  to  $\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}$  for  $\forall \mu \in [M]$  but (2)  $\{\operatorname{rt}_{1,\operatorname{in}}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]} \neq \operatorname{com}$ . Let proof :=  $(\{\operatorname{rt}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}, \{\mathbb{T}^{\mu:\nu}\}_{\mu,\nu \in [M]})$  otherwise.
  - 4. Output (f, proof) as the proof.

{55}------------------------------------------------

Now, we show that  $C_4^*$  breaks the soundness of  $\langle C_4, R_4 \rangle$ . Recall that we assume for contradiction that  $C_5^*$  breaks the soundness of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ . Combined with the binding property of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ , this assumption implies that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com}) \leftarrow \langle \operatorname{C.Com}_5^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_5 \rangle$ , we have both Equation (I.1) and the following:

• either there exists  $i \in [n]$  such that

<span id="page-55-0"></span>
$$\Pr\left[x_i = \bot \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_5^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_5^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_5(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle\right] \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} , \tag{I.3}$$

• or there exists  $x_{\text{com}}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that we have Equation (I.2), but we also have

$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \land f(x_{\text{com}}^*) = 0 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q}_5; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_5^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D}_5(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \ge 1 - \frac{1}{M^2} + \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} \ . \tag{I.4}$$

Then, we consider two cases.

Case 1. First, we consider the case that for infinitely many  $\lambda$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(st_C,com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5 \rangle$ , we have Equations (I.1) and (I.3). Let  $\Lambda$  be the set of such  $\lambda$ . In this case, our goal is to obtain a contradiction by showing that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(st_C,com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_4^*, R.Com_4 \rangle$ , we have

<span id="page-55-4"></span><span id="page-55-1"></span>
$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \middle| \begin{array}{c} (Q, \mathsf{st}_R) \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.Q_4}; \ (f, \pi^*) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C, Q) \\ b \leftarrow \mathsf{R.Prv.D_4}(\mathsf{st}_R, \mathsf{com}, f, \pi^*) \end{array} \right] \ge \frac{1}{\lambda^c} , \tag{I.5}$$

and

<span id="page-55-3"></span>
$$\Pr\left[x_i = \bot \mid (\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_4^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_4(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle\right] \ge \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)} \ . \tag{I.6}$$

For any  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5 \rangle$ , let us say that  $(st_C, com)$  is good for  $C_5^*$  if Equations (I.1) and (I.3) hold w.r.t.  $(st_C, com)$ . Similarly, for any  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_4^*, R.Com_4 \rangle$ , let us say that  $(st_C, com)$  is good for  $C_4^*$  if  $st_C$  can be parsed as  $(com, com', st_C')$  such that  $(st_C', com')$  is good for  $C_5^*$ . From the assumption of this case, it follows that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$ , an execution of  $\langle C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5 \rangle$  produces good  $(st_C, com)$  with non-negligible probability. Hence, from the construction of  $C_4^*$ , it follows that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$ , an execution of  $\langle C.Com_4^*, R.Com_4 \rangle$  produces good  $(st_C, com)$  with non-negligible probability.

We first observe that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$  and an overwhelming fraction of good ( $\operatorname{st}_C$ ,  $\operatorname{com}$ ) for  $C_4^*$ , we have Equation (I.5). Toward this end, we make a sequence of observations.

- 1. First, for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$  and an overwhelming fraction of good  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$  for  $C_4^*$ , we have that  $\operatorname{st}_C$  can be parsed as  $(\operatorname{com}, \operatorname{com}', \operatorname{st}'_C)$  such that  $\operatorname{com} \neq \bot$ .

  This is because under that condition that an execution of  $\langle \operatorname{C.Com}_4^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_4 \rangle$  produces good  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$ , we have  $\operatorname{Pr}[b_{\operatorname{BAD}} = 0] \leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$  during the execution of  $\langle \operatorname{C.Com}_4^*, \operatorname{R.Com}_4 \rangle$  due to the receiver security of  $\operatorname{OT}(\operatorname{Definition} 12)$  and Equation  $(\operatorname{I.1})$ , which is guaranteed by the definition of good  $(\operatorname{st}_C, \operatorname{com})$ .
- 2. Next, for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$  and an overwhelming fraction of good (st<sub>C</sub>, com) for  $C_4^*$ , we have both of the following.
  - $\operatorname{st}_C$  can be parsed as  $(\operatorname{com}, \operatorname{com}', \operatorname{st}'_C)$  such that  $\operatorname{com} \neq \bot$ .
  - The probability that  $C.Prv_4^*(st_C)$  outputs (f, proof) such that  $proof = \bot$  during an execution of  $\langle C.Prv_4^*(st_C), R.Prv_4(com) \rangle$  is negligible.

This is because of the above observation and the binding property of SHCom.

3. Finally, for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$  and an overwhelming fraction of good ( $\mathsf{st}_C$ ,  $\mathsf{com}$ ) for  $C_4^*$ , we have Equation (I.5). This is because of the above observation and the receiver security of OT. Indeed, if Equation (I.5) does not hold for non-negligible fraction of good ( $\mathsf{st}_C$ ,  $\mathsf{com}$ ) for  $C_4^*$ , one can break the receiver security of OT (Definition 12) by emulating an execution of  $\langle \mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C), \mathsf{R.Prv}_4(\mathsf{com}) \rangle$  since the internally emulated  $\mathsf{C.Prv}_5^*(\mathsf{st}_C)$  satisfies Equation (I.1).

We next observe that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$  and a non-negligible fraction of good (st<sub>C</sub>, com) for  $C_4^*$ , we have Equation (I.6). This can be observed by combining the fact that an execution of

<span id="page-55-2"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>34</sup>Specifically, the receiver security of OT and Equation (I.1) imply that during the execution of  $(C.Com_4^*, R.Com_4)$ , each trial for obtaining  $\{rt_{1,in}^{\mu}, dec_{sh}^{\mu}\}_{\mu \in [M]}$  succeeds with probability at least  $1/\lambda^c$ . Thus, from Marcov's inequality, the probability that all the  $T_{sh}$  trials fail is negligible.

{56}------------------------------------------------

- 1.  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_4^*, R.Com_4 \rangle$ ;
- 2.  $(\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_{A}^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_4(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle$

perfectly emulates an execution of

- 1.  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow \langle C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5 \rangle$ ;
- 2.  $(\bot, x_i) \leftarrow \langle E_5^{\mathsf{C.Prv}_5^*(\mathsf{st}_C, \cdot)}(\mathsf{com}, i), \mathsf{R.Dec}_5(\mathsf{com}, i) \rangle$

(where the first step of  $E_5$  in the latter execution is emulated in the commit phase in the former execution), and the fact that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$  and any good (st<sub>C</sub>, com) for  $C_5^*$ , we have Equation (I.3).

By combining what is observed in the above two paragraphs, we conclude that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C.Com}_4^*, \mathsf{R.Com}_4 \rangle$ , we have Equations (I.5) and (I.6) as desired.

**Case 2.** We next consider the case that for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(st_C, com) \leftarrow (C.Com_5^*, R.Com_5)$ , we have Equation (I.1) and the following.

• There exists  $x_{\text{com}}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that we have Equation (I.2), but we also have Equation (I.4).

Let  $\Lambda$  be the set of such  $\lambda$ . In this case, our goal is to obtain a contradiction by showing that for  $\forall \lambda \in \Lambda$ , with non-negligible probability over the choice of  $(\mathsf{st}_C, \mathsf{com}) \leftarrow \langle \mathsf{C.Com}_4^*, \mathsf{R.Com}_4 \rangle$ , we have Equations (I.5) and the following.

• There exists  $x_{\text{COM}}^* := (x_1^*, \dots, x_n^*) \in \{0, 1\}^n$  such that we have Equation (H.2), but we also have

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{c|c}b=1\\ \land f(x_{\text{com}}^*)=0\end{array}\middle|\begin{array}{c}(Q,\mathsf{st}_R)\leftarrow\mathsf{R.Prv.Q_4};\ (f,\pi^*)\leftarrow\mathsf{C.Prv}_4^*(\mathsf{st}_C,Q)\\ b\leftarrow\mathsf{R.Prv.D_4}(\mathsf{st}_R,\mathsf{com},f,\pi^*)\end{array}\right]\geq\frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)}\ . \tag{I.7}$$

The proof for this case is similar to the proof for Case 1. Specifically, we can show that Equation (I.1) implies Equation (I.5) as in Case 1, and we can also show that Equation (I.4) implies Equation (I.7) very similarly to Case 1.

By combining the analysis of the above two cases, we complete the proof of Lemma I.3.

## J ZK Scheme with Standard negl-Soundness

<span id="page-56-0"></span>As mentioned in Section 1.1, our constant-sound WI commit-and-prove protocol  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  in Appendix I can be transformed into a one that is zero-knowledge and negl-sound by using a variant of a transformation of Khurana et al. [KOS18]. For completeness, we briefly explain how  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  is transformed by it. (An overview of the transformation is given in [KOS18].)

#### J.1 Protocol Description

The transformation uses the following building blocks.

- <span id="page-56-1"></span>• A three-round commitment scheme two-com such that the committer commits to two values  $\hat{s}_0$ ,  $\hat{s}_1$  in the first round and then reveals them in the third round, and it is guaranteed that (1) one of the two commitments is binding while the other is equivocal, and (2) the receiver cannot tell which commitment is equivocal. Black-box constructions of such a commitment scheme are given in [ORS15, KOS18].
- A finite field G such that |G| is exponentially large.

We describe the transformed protocol  $\langle C_6, R_6 \rangle$  in Algorithm 21. (The only difference between the transformation that we use and the one given in [KOS18] is the definition of a in Round 2 of the prove phase, where in [KOS18], it is defined as  $a := x\alpha + r$  by viewing the committed value x as an element in G.

### J.2 Proof Sketch of Binding

The binding property follows from that of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ .

<span id="page-56-2"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>35</sup>Roughly speaking, we can still use the same security proof as Khurana et al. [KOS18] since, essentially, the only property that they use is that for any (x, r) and (x', r') such that  $x \neq x'$ , we have  $x\alpha + r \neq x'\alpha + r'$  with high probability when  $\alpha$  is chosen uniformly randomly.

{57}------------------------------------------------

**Algorithm 21** Commit Phase, Open Phase, and Prove Phase of  $\langle C_6, R_6 \rangle$ 

#### **Commit Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Com<sub>6</sub> runs  $hf_j \leftarrow R.Com_5$  for  $\forall j \in [\lambda]$  and then sends  $\{hf_j\}_{j \in [\lambda]}$  and the first-round message of two-com $(\hat{s}_0, \hat{s}_1)$  for randomly chosen  $\hat{s}_0, \hat{s}_1 \in \{0, 1\}^{\lambda}$ .

**Round 2:**  $C.Com_6$  does the following.

- 1. Choose random  $r \in G$  and  $s \in \{0, 1\}^{\lambda}$ , and let  $x'_{COM} := x_{COM} ||r|| s$ .
- 2. Run  $(com_j, st_C^j) \leftarrow C.Com_5(x'_{com}, hf)$  for  $\forall j \in [\lambda]$ .
- 3. Send  $\{com_j\}_{j\in[\lambda]}$  and the second-round message of two-com as the commitment.

.....

#### **Prove Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Prv.Q<sub>6</sub> runs  $(Q_j, \operatorname{st}_R^j) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Prv.Q}_5$  for  $j \in [\lambda]$ , and then sends  $\{Q_j\}_{j \in [\lambda]}$ , randomly chosen  $\alpha \in G$ , and the third-round message of two-com (which reveals  $\hat{s}_0$  and  $\hat{s}_1$ ) as the query.

**Round 2:**  $C.Prv_6$  does the following.

- 1. Compute  $a = x_n \alpha^n + \cdots + x_1 \alpha + r$  (in the field G), where  $x_i$  is the i-th bit of  $x_{\text{COM}}$ .
- 2. Run  $\pi_j \leftarrow \text{C.Prv}_5(\text{st}_C^j, \hat{f}, Q_j)$  for  $\forall j \in [\lambda]$ , where the function  $\hat{f}$  checks, given input  $x'_{\text{COM}} = x_{\text{COM}} || r || s$ , whether it holds

$$(f(x) = 1 \land x_n \alpha^n + \dots + x_1 \alpha + r = a) \lor (s = \hat{s}_0 \lor s = \hat{s}_1) .$$

3. Send *a* and  $\{\pi_i\}_{i\in[\lambda]}$  as the proof.

**Verification:** R.Prv.D<sub>6</sub> outputs 1 if and only if R.Prv.D<sub>5</sub>( $\operatorname{st}_R^j$ ,  $\operatorname{com}_j$ ,  $\hat{f}$ ,  $\pi_j$ ) = 1 for  $\forall j \in [\lambda]$ .

-

#### **Open Phase**

**Round 1:** R.Dec.Q<sub>6</sub> runs  $(Q_j, \operatorname{st}_R^j) \leftarrow \operatorname{R.Dec.Q}_5(i)$  for  $\forall j \in [\lambda]$  and sends  $\{Q_j\}_{j \in [\lambda]}$  and the third-round message of two-com as the query.

**Round 2:** C.Dec<sub>6</sub> runs  $\text{dec}_j \leftarrow \text{C.Dec}_5(\text{st}_C^j, Q_j)$  for  $\forall j \in [\lambda]$  and sends  $\{\text{dec}_j\}_{j \in [\lambda]}$  as the decommitment.

**Verification:** R.Dec.D<sub>6</sub> does the following.

- 1. Check whether there exists  $x_i$  such that it holds  $\mathsf{R.Dec.D}_5(\mathsf{st}_R^j,\mathsf{com}_j,\mathsf{dec}_j) = x_i$  for more than  $\lambda/2$  values of  $j \in [\lambda]$ .
- 2. Output  $x_i$  as the decommitted value if such  $x_i$  exists, and output  $\perp$  otherwise.

#### J.3 Proof Sketch of Zero-knowledge

The proof of zero-knowledge proceeds identically with that given in [KOS18]. Specifically, it suffices to consider a simulator that first obtains the values  $\hat{s}_0$ ,  $\hat{s}_1$  in Round 1 of the prove phase and then uses them to simulate the receiver's view in the commit and prove phases by relying on rewinding techniques.

#### <span id="page-57-0"></span>J.4 Proof Sketch of Soundness

The proof of soundness proceeds essentially identically with that given in [KOS18]. Specifically, we prove it by considering an extractor that applies the extractor  $E_5$  of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  for each instance of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  in the prove phase. Given this extractor, it suffices to show the following.

- <span id="page-57-1"></span>1. The extraction succeeds in most instances of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ .
- 2. Any cheating committer cannot prove false statements on the extracted value in most instances of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ .
- 3. The values extracted from most instances of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  are equal.

The first two can be shown by following the analysis of  $E_5$  (Lemma I.3). Specifically, the receiver security of OT guarantees that in at least  $\lambda - \omega(\log \lambda)$  instances of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$ , all the values that are committed by SBCom (e.g., decommitments to the hash of the initial MPC states) are correctly generated with non-negligible probability, and thus we can reuse the analysis of  $E_5$ . The last one can be shown by noticing that if different values,  $x_{\text{COM}} || r || s$  and  $x'_{\text{COM}} || r' || s'$  such that  $x_{\text{COM}} \neq x'_{\text{COM}}$ , are extracted, then with overwhelming probability over the choice of  $\alpha \in G$ , it holds  $x_n \alpha^n + \cdots + x_1 \alpha + r \neq x'_n \alpha^n + \cdots + x'_1 \alpha + r'$  (which implies that we have either  $x_n \alpha^n + \cdots + x_1 \alpha + r \neq a$  or  $x'_n \alpha^n + \cdots + x'_1 \alpha + r' \neq a$ ) and hence the cheating committer is required to prove a false statement in an instance of  $\langle C_5, R_5 \rangle$  unless it can break the security of two-com.

{58}------------------------------------------------

## K Lemmas from Kalai et al. [KRR14] and Subsequent Works

We give several lemmas that are based on those given in Kalai et al. [KRR14] and subsequent works. All the lemmas in this section can be trivially extended for the parallel setting that we consider in Appendix E (i.e., the setting where  $\mathcal{A}$  takes multiple sets of queries and outputs multiple functions).

#### K.1 Lemmas on SelfCorr

For each  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , let F, H, m,  $m_{10}$  be the parameters of our PCP system (PCP.P, PCP.V), and let D(X),  $D(X^{\xi})$ ,  $D(X^{\xi}_{1,\text{in}})$  be defined as in Section D.2.2. Let  $\zeta = \omega(\log \lambda)$ . Let LD-Test and SelfCorr be the algorithms that are defined in Algorithm 6 and Algorithm 1.

<span id="page-58-0"></span>Then, there exists a polynomial<sup>36</sup>  $\kappa_1 = O(\lambda |F|^2)$  such that for any  $\kappa_1$ -CNS adversary  $\mathcal{A}$ , the following lemmas hold. In the following, unless otherwise specified, we use (d, D) to denote any of  $(m|H|, D(X)), ((m-1)|H|, D(X^{\xi})),$  and  $(m_{10}|H|, D(X^{\xi}_{1 \text{ in}})).$ 

Lemma K.1 (Correctness of SelfCorr). If it holds

$$\Pr \left[ b = 1 \;\middle|\; b \leftarrow \mathsf{LD-Test}_{d,D,\zeta}^{\mathcal{A}} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$

<span id="page-58-1"></span>for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$  (let  $\Lambda$  be the set of such  $\lambda$ ), then there exists a negligible function  $\epsilon$  such that for every sufficiently large  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and  $\forall q \in D$ , it holds

$$\Pr\left[\tilde{A}(q) = \bot \ \middle| \ (\mathsf{out}, \tilde{A}) \leftarrow \mathsf{SelfCorr}_{d,D}^{\mathcal{A}}(\{q\}) \right] \leq \epsilon(\lambda) \ \ .$$

*Proof*. See [KRR13, Theorem 7.27] or [BHK16, Lemma 8].

Lemma K.2 (Consistency of SelfCorr). If it holds

$$\Pr\left[b = 1 \mid b \leftarrow \mathsf{LD-Test}_{d,D,\zeta}^{\mathcal{A}}\right] \ge 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$
,

<span id="page-58-2"></span>for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$  (let  $\Lambda$  be the set of such  $\lambda$ ), then there exists a negligible function  $\epsilon$  such that for every sufficiently large  $\lambda \in \Lambda$  and  $\forall q \in D$ , it holds

$$\Pr\begin{bmatrix} \tilde{A}_0(q) \neq \tilde{A}_1(q) & (Q_b, \mathsf{st}_b) \leftarrow \mathsf{SelfCorr}. \mathsf{Q}_D(\{q\}) \ \textit{for} \ \forall b \in \{0, 1\} \\ (\mathsf{out}, A) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(Q_0 \cup Q_1) \\ \tilde{A}_b \coloneqq \mathsf{SelfCorr}. \mathsf{Rec}_d(\mathsf{st}_b, A) \ \textit{for} \ \forall b \in \{0, 1\} \end{bmatrix} \leq \epsilon(\lambda)$$

*Proof sketch.* This can be proven by slightly modifying the proofs of [KRR13, Theorem 7.27] and [BHK16, Lemma 8]. Specifically, by inspection, one can see that these proofs consider, very roughly speaking, a modified version of SelfCorr that chooses  $2\lambda$  lines  $L_{0,1}, \ldots, L_{0,\lambda}, L_{1,1}, \ldots, L_{1,\lambda}$  for each query (instead of choosing  $\lambda$  lines), and then show that

- 1. the same value  $c_i$  is recovered by self-correction from  $L_{0,i}$  and  $L_{1,i}$  for most  $i \in [\lambda]$ , and
- 2. there exists a single value c such that it holds  $c_i = c$  for most  $i \in [\lambda]$ .

Hence, it follows that the same value is recovered by self-correction from most of the  $2\lambda$  lines, and thus, when those  $2\lambda$  lines are considered to be chosen from two instances of SelfCorr, the values that are recovered from them are the same. (For a formal argument, see [Kiy18, Claim 3].)

**Lemma K.3.** For each  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ , let  $(m_0, d_0, D_0) := (m, m|\mathbf{H}|, D(X))$  and let  $(m_1, d_1, D_1)$  be either  $(m - 1, (m - 1)|\mathbf{H}|, D(X^{\xi}))$  or  $(m_{io}, m_{io}|\mathbf{H}|, D(X^{\xi}_{1,in}))$ .

Assume that the following hold for infinitely many  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$  and let  $\Lambda$  be the set of such  $\lambda$ .

<span id="page-58-3"></span>• Low-degree Test on  $D_b$  ( $b \in \{0, 1\}$ ): For  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds

$$\Pr \left[ b = 1 \mid b \leftarrow \mathsf{LD-Test}_{d_b, D_b, \zeta}^{\mathcal{A}} \right] \ge 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$
.

- Low-degree Test, conditioned on  $L(0) \in D_1$ : It holds b = 1 with probability at least  $1 \text{negl}(\lambda)$  in the following probabilistic experiment.
  - 1. Choose  $\lambda$  random lines  $L_1, \ldots, L_{\lambda} : \mathbf{F} \to D_0$  such that each  $L \in \{L_1, \ldots, L_{\lambda}\}$  satisfies  $L(0) \in D_1$ .
  - 2.  $Run (out, A) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(Q)$ , where  $Q = \{L_j(t)\}_{j \in [\lambda], t \in F}$ .
